Full Text of the Fourth Plenary Session Declaration

National Consciousness Will Dominate the Future of National Affairs

Concentrate National Strength, Replenish National Power, Save the Nation and Seek Survival

Unite Sincerely and Accomplish the Great Task of Revolution and National Salvation

(Nanjing) The full text of the declaration of the Fourth Plenary Session of the Fourth Central Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang is as follows: Our Party held the Fourth Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee in the capital this time to review past work and examine future policies. Amidst pain and vigilance, we deeply feel that the past year since the Third Plenary Session has been a period of extreme internal and external difficulties. During this year, our Party and the people of the whole country have experienced unprecedented hardships in dealing with these successive changes. However, this process of hardship and struggle has given us an important revelation, that is, the great power of national consciousness will dominate everything. The future of national affairs and the revolutionary mission of our Party have coincided with the aspirations of the people of the whole country. This is what all the participants in this plenary session are inspired by, and it is also what they cannot fail to use as a source of encouragement. Tracing back to the time when the Japanese army occupied the three northeastern provinces, in January last year, there was the alarm at Yuguan, followed by the loss of Rehe. In the battles of Xifengkou, Lengkou, and Gubeikou, our soldiers braved the power of aircraft and heavy artillery, fought bloody battles, and defended their positions. More than 40,000 people were killed or wounded, and the loss of civilian lives was even more incalculable. This kind of heroic and tragic battle is rarely seen in the history of our country. This fully proves that the reason why our country has failed to achieve the goal of resisting humiliation and avenging its shame is due to the lack of national strength, but the morale of the soldiers is actually very useful. However, the reason for creating this heroic record is the mobilization of the national consciousness of defending the country with death. When the war in the north was tense, the bandit suppression troops were urgently mobilized, causing the dying Red bandits to take the opportunity to break through and run rampant again. However, since the encirclement and suppression plan was continuously implemented, all the soldiers were filled with righteous indignation and fought with twice the usual vigor. They repeatedly defeated the main force of the bandits, recovered important areas, and the effect of annihilation can be expected soon. The expectation and encouragement of the people of the whole country for the bandit suppression military operations are also unprecedented. This also fully proves that the Red bandits' conspiracy to use foreign troubles to endanger the nation and the race has only strengthened the reaction of the deep national consciousness of our military and civilians throughout the country. The victory of the bandit suppression military operations has already reached the point of success. However, Chen Li Nuo, a rebellious traitor in Fujian, suddenly lost his mind at this time and launched a rebellion to destroy the Party and abandon the country, with the aim of frightening people and shaking the foundation of the country. However, as soon as the banner of rebellion was raised, the whole country condemned it. The pseudo-government in Fuzhou was in danger in less than ten days and collapsed in less than a month. The advocacy of the rebellion was extremely bizarre, and the suppression was also unprecedentedly swift. On the day when the national army recovered Fuzhou, the national emblem of the blue sky and white sun flew all over the city, and the enthusiasm of the people to welcome it was truly like seeing the light again. This especially shows that the Three People's Principles of saving the country, left by the late Premier Sun Yat-sen, are the true sustenance of the entire nation's life. Anyone who is ignorant of this principle and vainly hopes to make a plan for self-harm and self-destruction, once in contact with the vigorous and fiery national consciousness, will not fail to be defeated and destroyed. Looking back on the past year, every time the country encounters a crisis of survival, the potential national consciousness of the whole country will exert its great power once. We would like to express our highest respect and condolences to the soldiers who sacrificed themselves for the country in the battles of resisting humiliation, suppressing bandits, and quelling rebellions. Reflecting on the past, we feel even more that in this year, the composure and firmness of the will of the people of the whole country, the clarity and correctness of their understanding, and their ability to maintain order and make arduous progress in the state of national hardship and rural decline are sufficient to be a guarantee for the revival of our country. This conclusion is especially to be presented to the whole Party and the whole country as a source of inspiration and uprising. The great plan of saving the country and seeking survival has myriad aspects, but it can be summarized into the following two guidelines: First, it is not enough to save the country and seek survival without concentrating national strength. Second, it is not enough to save the country and seek survival without replenishing national power. This is generally recognized by all enlightened people in the country, and it is also what our Party has been committed to over the years. Looking at the changes in national affairs and the trends in the international situation, we are even more convinced that these two major prerequisites are absolutely necessary to be realized. In modern times, the first element of nation-building is to make the country respond from head to tail and connect branches and trunks to form a tightly organized machine. The second element is to make the country's blood circulate smoothly and its body full, forming a healthy machine both internally and externally. If either of these two elements is missing, or if there is organization but no strength, or if there is strength but no organization, then it will not be enough to stand on its own in the international community, nor will it be suitable as a tool to promote the interests of the people. Therefore, from the perspective of national politics, both unity and construction are absolutely necessary. Anything that hinders unity and construction is hindering the great plan of saving the country and seeking survival. From the perspective of the elements that make up the country, whether it is all the members of our Party or all the people of China, unity and effort are absolutely necessary. Anyone who cannot practice unity and effort is delaying the great plan of saving the country and seeking survival. The danger of the Chinese nation is extreme. Lost territory has not been recovered, and those who seek to harm us are now borrowing the remnants of the imperial system and falsely claiming titles. If we do not rise up quickly to consolidate national unity, complete all construction, and establish the foundation for resisting humiliation, the country will inevitably fall into fragmentation and be beyond salvation. Moreover, the international situation is already pressing us. Therefore, this meeting, after careful consideration, believes that what should be revealed today is the clear outline related to the foundation of the country. All the paths that the whole country has confirmed as unchangeable are the goals that all comrades of the Party and compatriots of the whole country should unite and work together to achieve. What the country expects from our Party is not about much talk. What our Party is painfully vigilant about and takes as its own responsibility is only to practice it. This meeting believes that at this time, we should use the spirit of not being arrogant and not being afraid of telling the truth, overcoming selfishness and uniting the masses, to strive to consolidate the foundation of the revolution and establish the foundation for saving the country. As for the decisions made by the previous meeting, whether they have been hindered in the middle and have not been implemented, or have been in progress and have not been completed, and the plans of this meeting on various facilities such as politics, military affairs, economy, education, and Party affairs, we vow to promote them with a consistent spirit and concrete steps. We hope that the sincere unity of all comrades of the Party will create the sincere unity of the people of the whole country and our Party. We hope that the hard work of all comrades of the Party will move the people of the whole country, and we will expect each other to make double efforts, self-purify and self-sacrifice, and do our best to be sincere. With one heart and one mind, we will reverse the dangerous situation. The survival and development of the country and the nation, and the completion of the great cause of revolution and national salvation must be sought in the unanimous sincerity and efforts of the whole country. This is the declaration. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 25th)

Current Affairs Commentary

Another Alarm in Xinjiang Shu

The largest central city in the southern part of the Tianshan Mountains in Xinjiang has recently undergone a huge change. With the support of Hui chieftains, a so-called new government has been established. The content of this new government is still vague and unclear, even according to Reuters and TASS. What is known on the surface now is: first, the leader of the new government is a Hui merchant; second, it seeks independence and separation from China; third, it excludes Han people; fourth, it sends representatives to unite with the Kingdom of Afghanistan; fifth, it invites Hui people exiled in India and Japan to train troops. All of these indicate the opinions of some Hui people in Xinjiang Province, and their words of expelling Han people are especially enough to stir up the emotions of the Hui people. They believe that this kind of proposition conforms to the nature of history and can confront the Han people and achieve the results of self-determination. However, they do not know that Xinjiang is located between two major powers, and the Hui people in Xinjiang are still in the era of agricultural economy and cannot compete with the commercial economy. Once independent, they will only be used by foreigners and will not realize that they will become a continuation of India.

Many of the Han officials serving in Xinjiang Province are stubborn in their thinking. Not only is there no construction in politics, but it also makes the local Hui people full of grievances, causing neighboring countries to have ambitious desires and often covet them. Regarding this rebellion of the Hui people, we are reluctant to make harsh criticisms at this time due to the remoteness of the roads, the obstruction of transportation, and the extreme alienation of the relationship between the two sides. However, today, the political hub of Xinjiang Province is still in the hands of the Han people. If the provincial government can know the importance of this matter and quickly respond with sincerity, even if it is not enough to quell the rebellion immediately, it may be possible to prevent the rebellion from expanding further, so as to seek recovery slowly.

The Xinjiang incident has been revealed for a long time, and the central government has also paid attention to this early on. It has twice sent senior officials to Xinjiang to conduct on-the-spot investigations into the causes of past changes in Xinjiang Province and the essential ways to design governance in the future. Huang Musong's comforting has become a thing of the past, and Luo Wengan's inspection has just returned. What they contribute to the central government must be practical and feasible plans. Therefore, when the Hui people's problem in the southern part of the country suddenly breaks out, the central government will surely have a plan in mind and there is no need for us to worry about it.

Xinjiang has an area of ​​5.36 million square miles and a population of approximately 2.5 to 3 million. Some argue that Xinjiang is entirely barren, with a sparse population and a climate that is not very suitable. However, in fact, the Gobi Desert only accounts for one-fifth of the total area of ​​Xinjiang Province. Its hindrance to the survival of the population and the obstruction of the development of transportation are also limited. However, due to the separation of the Tianshan Mountains, it is divided into the northern and southern parts, and both the northern and southern parts have rivers flowing through them, with abundant water and grass, which are suitable for both animal husbandry and farming. In the northern part of the Tianshan Mountains, although it is called severe cold, it is at most only 20 degrees below zero on the Fahrenheit scale, which is better than the climate of Heilongjiang Province. The reason why the population is sparse and transportation is inconvenient is because the country has never paid attention to the northwest. Moreover, the northern part of the Tianshan Mountains is becoming more and more tense due to the independence of Outer Mongolia and the success of the Soviet-Western Railway.

Now the dispute between Hui and Han has gone from secret brewing to exposure. From the surface observation, it does not seem to be very serious. However, due to the years of famine and military disasters in Xinjiang Province, if those ambitious countries add to the sowing of discord behind the scenes and take the opportunity to profit, the resulting changes are really difficult to predict. Therefore, we believe that whether the affair in Shule is true or not, the government should quickly make arrangements and announce the policy of governing Xinjiang, so that the Han people have something to rely on and the Hui people can realize it as soon as possible in order to reverse today's decline.

He and Yan Unanimously Advise Against the Sun-Ma Conflict

Sun's Army Approaches Ningxia Provincial City

Gansu and Qinghai Troops Reinforce Ningxia

Chairman Chiang Kai-shek Meets Representatives from Both Sun and Ma Sides

(Beiping) Sources familiar with the situation say that He and Yan have decided to mediate the Sun-Ma conflict. (Special telegram on the 25th)

Sun's representative, Wang Shouxin, visited He on the morning of the 25th. Wang Lun met with him on his behalf and informed him that the central government's telegram still charged the branch with handling the matter. He's intention was to hope that Sun's army could quickly withdraw to its original defense area and hand over Dengkou and the occupied territory of Ningxia Province to the 15th Route Army for defense, and then develop Woye for reclamation. On the 25th, neither side sent a telegram to Beiping, and the situation on the front line was unclear. (Special telegram on the 25th)

(Beiping) Hou Cheng, who was previously ordered to go to Taiyuan to meet with Yan Xishan, heard that the result was satisfactory. The Shanxi authorities are working hard to act as a third party to mediate and dissuade Sun's troops from advancing. As for the central government's handling of this matter, due to the facts, it must be carefully considered before a decision can be made. (Special telegram on the 25th)

(Beiping) Regarding the issue of Sun's troops advancing westward, the two armies are still confronting each other for days. The troops of Gansu and Qinghai provinces are now actively advancing. Japanese Military Strategy Against Russia According to a Certain Source

(Beiping) According to a certain source, there are frequent clashes between Japanese and Russian outposts in the Dongning area. The Japanese strategy against Russia is divided into three routes: central, left, and right. The left route is in the Dongning and Suifenhe area, with mostly defensive works. The central route runs from Heihe to Mohe, with the aim of crossing the Heilongjiang River from Mohe and cutting off the Siberian Railway. A large motor road between Heihe and Mohe has been built, with a width of 48 feet, and many stations have been set up along the road, which seems to be taking an offensive stance. The right route is in Manzhouli, also on the defensive. The three routes are commanded from Harbin, and the general station is also located there. This is the first phase of the war plan. The second phase is divided into offensive and defensive sections. If the central route wins, the right route will also take an offensive stance. If the three routes are defeated, a major battle will begin between Changchun and Shenyang. (Special telegram on the 25th)

(Beiping) Liu Guitang's remnants have fled to the area of Damingsha Cliff on the Yellow River. In addition to stationing troops in Daming to supervise the encirclement and suppression, He Zhuguo also ordered Yao Dongyong's troops to defend. The railway artillery team is responsible for protecting the road. Guo Xipeng's troops are suppressing Liu's bandits in She County, and Commander Dong was killed in battle. (Special telegram on the 25th)

Preparations for the Air Defense Research Association Are Largely Completed

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Military Affairs believes that the preparations for the Air Defense Research Class have been largely completed. The central government agencies should select 70 trainees and send a letter to each agency to register with the research class. After passing the review, they will be scheduled to take the exam and receive instruction. It is learned that each agency has decided to collect applications from ambitious staff members before February 10 and send them to the class for review. (Special telegram on the 25th)

The National Economic Commission Is Scheduled to Hold a Regular Meeting Tomorrow

(Nanjing) The third regular meeting of the National Economic Commission was originally scheduled to be held on the 26th, but it has now been rescheduled to the 27th because the 26th is the capital's welcome rally for the Central Committee members and Chiang Kai-shek's triumphant return. The meeting procedure will first be a report by Qin Fen, the secretary-general, on the preparations for the meeting, the work after its establishment, and the important cases that have been handled and not handled. Then, the various construction plans of the meeting will be discussed. (Special telegram on the 25th)

Xu Yuanquan Returns to Shashi

(Hankou) After completing his official duties in Hankou, Xu Yuanquan flew back to Shashi by plane on the 25th, arriving at noon. He will depart within days to Shihe to supervise the suppression of He Long's remnants and handle post-war recovery in the bandit areas. (Special telegram on the 25th)

Peng Weiren Telegraphs News of the Capture of the Lianhua Bandit Nest

(Nanjing) Peng Weiren telegraphed that the Lianhua Bandit Nest, which had been captured by bandits for several years, was captured, and many dying refugees were rescued. The pseudo-Hunan-Jiangxi Provincial Suiwantai Guerrilla Force and the scattered bandits in the pseudo-Hunan-Jiangxi Military Region attacked Taihe on the 20th, but were repelled by the militia. The bandits retreated to Yongxin. (Special telegram on the 25th)

(Nanchang) Dai Fusheng, a bandit from Donghuangpi, Yihuang, led 300 armed bandits, four mortars, and one generator to surrender. The county magistrate approved the formation of a volunteer team. (Special telegram on the 25th)

The Jiangxi Headquarters Delimits Various Garrison Areas

Statistics of Fortifications in the Province

(Nanchang) The headquarters has delimited various garrison areas: (1) The Eastern Jiangxi Area, including 14 counties in Xinyu, Raohe, and Guangxin; (2) The Ganjiang Area, along the Ganjiang River, from Xiajiang to Wan'an; (3) The area east of the Ganjiang River, including Yongfeng, Xingan, and Chongren; (4) The area from Linchuan and Nancheng to Nanfeng; (5) The area around Jinxi and Zixi. Xing Zhennan, Mao Bingwen, Zhou Hunyuan, and other commanders are supervising the post-war recovery and preventing bandits from fleeing back. (Special telegram on the 24th)

(Nanchang) According to statistics from the provincial government, in addition to the bridgehead fortifications on the open roads, the military has built 1,500 fortifications and the people have built 1,400. Construction is still underway. Each fortification can hold 500 soldiers. (Special telegram on the 24th)

The Case of Stolen Antiques from the Shandong Library Was Solved Immediately After It Occurred

The Thief, Si Zhengmin, Has Been Arrested and All Stolen Antiques Have Been Recovered

(Jinan) Seventy-one antiques, worth more than 100,000 yuan, were stolen from the art exhibition room of the Provincial Library at 4 am on the 22nd. Han ordered the Public Security Bureau to strictly arrest the thief. The thief's name is Si Zhengmin. After stealing the items that night, because there were too many to carry, he sank three Ming porcelain Longquan plates into Daming Lake outside the museum. When he went to retrieve them at 6:30 pm on the 24th, he was caught on the spot by Zhao Shiqi, a patrol officer of the Public Security Bureau of the museum. He was taken to his house to search for the stolen goods, but nothing was found. Now, he is being questioned in detail at the Public Security Bureau. His wife, Liu, confessed that they were hidden in the attic of the living room, where the tiles were lifted up, put in, and covered again. He was then taken back to search for the stolen goods, and they were all recovered without missing a single item. Si confessed that he used to be a worker at the Electric Light Company. After joining the Communist Party, he surrendered and became a member of the Anti-Communist Team of the Provincial Party Headquarters. Later, he was expelled and is now unemployed. He climbed over the wall alone that night. The people in the museum had not yet slept and were hiding in the women's restroom. He opened the door and entered to steal the items after four hours. Han decided to interrogate him personally tomorrow morning and then execute him. Among the stolen items, the Wucai Wanli Porcelain Vase, the Song White Porcelain Incense Burner, the Song Mingquan Burner, the Jiajing Plain Yellow Plate (eight in total), and the Tang Dynasty handwritten scriptures are all worth a lot of money. There were Song and Yuan version samples in the room, but Si knew they were samples and useless, so he only stole the copied and unique versions. (Special telegram on the 25th)

Chen Zongcheng Summons Representatives of Workers in Beiping for Talks

(Beiping) Chen Zongcheng summoned representatives of workers from factories all over the city for talks at the auditorium of the Social Affairs Bureau at 2 pm on the 25th and inquired in detail about the labor situation. More than 30 representatives from the Tram Workers' Union, Danhua Match Factory, Beer Company, etc. attended. Chen Ponong, the section chief of the Social Affairs Bureau, was present. Chen first described the nature of the International Labor Office and his purpose in coming to the north to investigate. He hoped that the representatives would report on the actual situation of the workers in detail so that they could study it together. Then, each representative reported one by one. Chen finally encouraged them with three points: (1) The International Labor Office is very concerned about the labor movement in China and is willing to cooperate with China to seek to increase happiness and strive to the end. (2) Chinese workers have always had the virtues of being hardworking and enduring hardships, which are unmatched by other countries. They should maintain this spirit from beginning to end. (3) At this time when the country is in great distress and the labor movement should be improved, it is hoped that they will unite and obey the government's guidance to deal with the difficulties with their entire strength. The representatives were very excited. The meeting lasted for two hours. According to Chen, the impression he got from this inspection was very good. The workers' lives are already hard, and the working hours are long. It is really necessary to improve this in the future. The International Labor Office is very willing to help the Chinese labor movement and improve the lives of workers. After Chen goes to Tianjin next week, he will return to Shanghai to prepare to attend this year's International Labor Conference. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 25th)

Discovery of Japanese Kidnappers in Fengrun

(Tianjin) According to a report from a certain government agency in this city, Zheng Jiugao, a resident of Wangjia Village in Fengrun County, and the wealthiest man in the county, was suddenly confronted by four Japanese and three Chinese accomplices at 8 a.m. on the 25th. They drove a large cart straight to the village's security team headquarters. They drew pistols and searched for Zheng Jiugao. The bandits opened fire and resisted arrest. After an hour-long battle, the bandits were overwhelmed and completely captured. Progress in Technical Cooperation Between League of Nations and China

Secretary-General Issues Report

(Geneva) League of Nations Secretary-General Joseph Avenol issued a report today outlining the progress of technical cooperation between the League of Nations and China in the areas of health, transportation, and transit, as well as on economic, financial, cultural, and administrative matters. The report stated that League of Nations experts were working closely with Chinese authorities with remarkable results, especially the three-year plan to reorganize health affairs, which included establishing hospitals in the capital and forming mobile medical teams. The report specifically mentioned the Shanghai anti-cholera vaccination program, stating that cholera has now been eradicated in Shanghai. In 1932, over one million people in Shanghai were vaccinated. Regarding road construction and water conservancy projects, the report stated that great efforts are underway, the most notable being the highway system. A total of 1,405 kilometers of highways have been built in Anhui, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang provinces, connecting to Shanghai and linking with over 2,000 kilometers of existing highways. The road construction program envisions building 22,000 kilometers of new roads, with the project divided into five phases. The report also mentioned assistance to the silk industry, public screenings of educational films, administrative improvements, and the reorganization of telegraph and telephone services. (Reuters dispatch, 25th)

Great Fog in London

City in Darkness, Trains Crash, Traffic Halted

(London) A heavy fog fell today in the London suburbs, the worst in years. Accidents occurred frequently, with thirty-seven known injuries. Reports of further incidents continue to arrive. The fog began at 3 a.m. and thickened an hour later. By 8 a.m., all of London was exceptionally dark. Workers were idled due to transportation disruptions. Some workers, unable to reach their offices, returned home to rest. Later, there was a heavy frost, making the streets extremely slippery. Some people were even seen ice skating in the streets. A transport truck, a bicycle, and five other vehicles collided in one location. Trains continued to operate as usual, but were later delayed due to the adverse weather. By 11 a.m., the fog covered all of London like a blanket, extending as far as 60 miles to Kent, Surrey, and Southampton. Visibility was limited to ten or fifteen yards. The small ferries across the Thames attempted to operate, but were forced to suspend service due to the weather. In the afternoon, the fog seemed to abate slightly in central London, but increased again at night. All parking areas in the city were full, as drivers, deeming the roads too slippery, parked their cars and took the subway home. (Reuters dispatch, 24th)

(London) Four people have died and hundreds injured in collisions caused by the Great Fog in London. (Reuters dispatch, 25th)

Trends in Japanese Politics: Diet Thwarts Military Faction's Power

House of Representatives Resolutely Attacks Military Interference in Politics

A Change Since the Assassination of Inukai Tsuyoshi

(Tokyo) In the Seiyukai's first day of interpellation speeches, Tokonami Takejiro fired a major salvo, strongly advocating for the unification of political parties to uphold parliamentary politics. On the second day, Ando Masazumi went a step further, pressing the military on the issue of the military's statement that was sowing discord between the military and the people. Shimada Toshio also issued a warning to Prime Minister Saito and Hatoyama Fumio regarding this issue, attacking the military. The military's camp was unexpectedly weak in response, creating a deep sense that the military could be swayed. The Seiyukai is secretly celebrating its victory and plans to pursue the attack further in the budget committee. However, some believe that pressing the advantage too far would provoke the military's emotions, intensify the conflict between political parties and the military, and potentially lead to unfortunate incidents. Therefore, it remains to be seen whether they will continue the pursuit or stop at this point. The trend is highly noteworthy. (Dentsu dispatch, 25th)

(Tokyo) In this session of the Diet, the atmosphere in the House of Representatives is extremely tense, with Seiyukai representative Tokonami's speech advocating for parliamentary politics and Minseito representative Machida Chuji's advocacy of constitutionalism. Furthermore, Ando Masazumi's speech regarding the division between the military and the people had the effect of warning the military against rash actions. In the past, the Diet's approach to military issues was to abandon its right to deliberate on national affairs and simply go through the motions. However, in this session, the Diet is freely expressing opinions and deliberating on military issues. The intention is not to overthrow the military or oppose the military, but to uphold parliamentary politics. The efforts of the parties, whose credibility was damaged after the May 15th Incident, to restore their credibility can be seen here. (United Press dispatch, 25th)

(Tokyo) Tokonami Takejiro, a leader of the Seiyukai, strongly advocated for upholding constitutionalism at the beginning of his interpellation speech, while simultaneously advocating for the necessity of a united front among political parties. Machida Chuji, representing the Minseito in the House of Representatives on the 24th, expressed agreement with Tokonami's views. Finally, he added that in this difficult situation, cooperation among political parties to achieve a stronger and more powerful national policy is the most urgent task, thereby clarifying the party's position. This is further promoting an atmosphere of cooperation between the ruling and opposition parties, which is attracting considerable attention from all quarters. (Dentsu dispatch, 25th)

Fierce Interpellations in the House of Representatives

Jealousy of Our Country's Air Force Development

Saito Does Not View the Current Situation Optimistically

Will the Military No Longer Interfere in Politics?

(Tokyo) The third day of the House of Representatives convened at 1:28 p.m. First, Hachisuka Saburo took the podium to discuss the Navy's Second Supplementary Plan, as follows:

For future disarmament conferences, fundamental countermeasures should be established. As for appearances, there have been many failures and few gains, such as the London Treaty. Is there any intention to revise or abandon it?

He also said, "There is the fact that American capital has invaded China's aviation industry. What are the authorities' views on this?"

Naval Minister Osumi rose to respond:

From the perspective of national defense security, we are carefully studying the fundamental principles of disarmament treaties or conferences, etc.

As for the development of the air forces of our neighbors, China and the Soviet Union, our countermeasures should be practical and effective. The government is also working hard to study this.

Next, Ogawa Gotaro took the podium and raised the following questions:

If a budget that favors military spending is implemented, it will only make the military-industrial complex more prosperous and have nothing to do with revitalizing rural areas. As a result, rural and urban areas will not be able to share the benefits equally. This unfairness is extreme. Is it ultimately the military's intention to strengthen the current capitalist system?

He also discussed the issue of military discipline as follows:

Regarding military interference in politics and political opinions of military personnel, what are the military authorities' thoughts on this?

He further discussed financial and economic issues as follows:

Does the meaning of the so-called "inconvenient to state" tax increase period mean that it will not be implemented in 1935? Before the occurrence of a disastrous inflation, is it necessary to carry out a comprehensive tax increase?

He also discussed other trade relations and trade balance policies, demanding a response from the government. Finance Minister Takahashi rose to reply:

Regarding the idea of imposing a special tax on military industrialists, the intention is that after the tax increase, the national finances will improve. However, on the other hand, there will also be the issue of not being able to avoid issuing deficit bonds, so it is better not to do it.

If taxes are not raised temporarily for a year or two, the people will have the resources to be active, so it is not advisable to be too drastic.

Next, Naval Minister Osumi replied:

Military personnel currently in service are prohibited from interfering in politics and should abide by this. If there are illegal military personnel in this regard, they should be dealt with. It goes without saying. However, military personnel, even in active service, cannot help but be concerned about politics, which influences national power. It cannot be said that it is unreasonable for them to cultivate political common sense in this sense.

Then, Army Minister Hayashi spoke as follows:

The procurement of military supplies is also carried out by industrialists below the middle class. National defense and politics are inseparable. Therefore, it is a natural and reasonable occurrence that those who are overly concerned about national defense may rise up to study politics or make political arguments. It cannot be said that this never happens. Ogawa further questioned:

According to the answers given by the Army and Navy Ministers, their tone seems to approve of military interference in politics. What is the Prime Minister's view on this answer?

Prime Minister Saito rose to reply:

There is nothing unreasonable in the answers given by the two ministers.

The Army Minister added:

My answer did not mean to approve of interference.

After this explanation, Ogawa's questioning came to an end. Next, Haraguchi of the Seiyukai began questioning: "Observing the current international situation, armaments are certainly necessary. However, under the pretext of an emergency, military spending has been abnormally increased, and the people cannot but have doubts. How will this be explained?" This was an investigation into the military budget problem, which Finance Minister Takahashi will answer. Afterwards, Nakano Seigo began questioning with sharp arguments, and the atmosphere in the Diet became tense. The gist of his questions is recorded as follows:

The Prime Minister and other cabinet members have very different understandings of the current situation. The Foreign Minister often uses "crisis" as a catchphrase, and responds handsomely to the recent pronouncements of the great powers. Does he ultimately have the determination to adjust the essence of diplomacy? Please respond. Regarding the issue with Soviet Russia, there is a sense of relying on something without fear. Is there an active passion to resolve the issue with the Soviets? Please also answer clearly.

Regarding the recognition of stabilizing the financial world, can a semi-administrative and semi-judicial industrial inspection agency be established, modeled after the U.S. Federal Trade Commission? Is there such an intention? Next, regarding the agricultural issue, he launched a more intense barrage at the government. Then he talked about financial issues, and his conclusion was as follows:

The crisis is not limited to 1936. There must be epoch-making reforms to deal with it. Currently, our country's trade is suffering from the blows of the combined economy, and the situation has not improved. Therefore, there are export control measures and production control organizations. But how to reconcile production control with the welfare of the masses? This leads to the necessity of financial control and the need to establish an economic general staff headquarters. Self-sufficiency within the country is not the spirit of a newly emerging Japan. In an emergency, there are unavoidable circumstances. In this situation, what is the understanding of the cabinet members?

Nakano's questions lasted for more than an hour and a half. Finally, Prime Minister Saito replied:

The government is not optimistic about the current situation and should work together with the people of the whole country to overcome the difficulties.

Afterwards, no ministers responded. Nakano again took the podium to demand a response, and the Diet became agitated. Foreign Minister Hirota then made a brief explanation:

In today's complex international relations, it seems appropriate not to make extreme remarks. We should be careful in this matter.

Later, Commerce Minister Nakajima responded, and the meeting adjourned. (United Press dispatch, 25th)

The House of Peers Will Follow Up

Questioning on Military Discipline Issues

(Tokyo) Regarding the previous statement issued by the military regarding the movement to sow discord between the military and the people, Prime Minister Saito stated in his reply in the House of Representatives that he was completely unaware of it and considered it unexpected, and that the motivation for its publication was very weak. After consultations between various factions, the truth will be investigated, and an urgent interpellation will be raised at an appropriate opportunity. (Dentsu dispatch, 25th)

(Tokyo) Kensei Nao, a member of the Upper House, has decided to raise impeachment-like questions to Prime Minister Saito, Education Minister Hatoyama, Naval Minister Osumi, and Army Minister Hayashi regarding thought problems and the revival of discipline and military discipline. The Diet atmosphere regarding this discipline issue is quite tense, and the government may not be allowed to rest easy. (Dentsu dispatch, 25th)

Hirota and Wakatsuki in Agreement

Japanese People Feel Like They Have Taken a Cooling Medicine

(Tokyo) The Minseito believes that Foreign Minister Hirota's response to Machida Chuso's question regarding the international crisis of 1935 is completely consistent with the opinions normally held by President Wakatsuki. Hirota's response this time can dispel the concerns of the people, and social unrest can be naturally eliminated as a result. (United Press dispatch, 25th)

Italian Public Opinion Ridicules Hirota

Engaging in Aggression in the Name of Peace

Japan's Untrustworthiness Has Alerted Britain and the United States

Europe Should Unite to Deal with the Far East Problem

Rome: It is reported that the Japanese ambassador to Rome has been instructed by his government to make a friendly recommendation to the Italian government regarding Italian newspaper commentaries on Japan. The Japanese government is particularly concerned about an article by Italian Prime Minister Mussolini recently published in Hearst newspapers. Simultaneously, Italian newspapers are no longer silent about Foreign Minister Hirota's speech on the opening day of the Diet, and are publishing articles evaluating and refuting Japan's claim to be a pillar of peace in the Far East. Tavoncetti, a reporter for the important Fascist assembly's "Tribune" wrote an article containing mockery, stating that the result of Japan's advocacy of peace has been that the United States has decided to build 120 warships, and that the British, Australian, and New Zealand representatives expressed panic at the naval conference in Singapore. The article concludes by saying that the countries of Europe should urgently unite to deal with the Far East problem. (Reuters dispatch, 24th)

Rome: Several newspapers here have commented on Foreign Minister Hirota's recent speech in the House of Peers. The Labor Newspaper of the Pan-fascist Party concludes, "Is the Japanese-style peace the only possible peace in East Asia?" The newspaper quotes the words Hirota used to explain his so-called peace policy, comparing them with the facts in the Far East, and states that according to Hirota, what Japan seeks can be summarized as peace. However, Japan's plans to expand its influence continue unabated. When Japan wants to conquer East Asia, any country that hinders its progress, by whatever means, is viewed by Japan as a threat to peace, preparing for war. As for the formal activities of the League of Nations Council, they cannot help but make people laugh. According to Hirota, after Japan withdrew from Geneva, "its commercial and diplomatic relations with other countries are closer and more amicable than before, which is fortunate." The "Tribune" then discusses the naval issues of Britain and the United States, stating that the United States has passed a bill to build 120 warships to strengthen the Navy in preparation for the naval treaty discussions in 1936, and Britain is concerned about ensuring the security of Australia and New Zealand, etc., because these places are sparsely populated and are the focus of Japanese imperialism, etc. (Havas dispatch, 24th)

A Troubled Autumn in Europe

France and Germany Disagree on Disarmament, Austria and Germany Face Friction Again

Austria Protests German Direction of National Socialist Movement

Will Bring Suit in League of Nations if Unsatisfied Response

(Berlin) Austria today formally lodged a diplomatic protest with Germany, stating that Germany should not secretly direct the Austrian National Socialist movement and declaring that if Germany's reply is not satisfactory to Austria, Austria will appeal to the League of Nations. According to reliable sources, it is expected that the German reply will not acknowledge this responsibility, so the League of Nations will soon encounter a major dispute again. (Reuters dispatch, 24th)

Germany Feigns Deafness and Muteness, Austrian Chancellor Reaches Point of Intolerance

(London) The fact that Austrian Chancellor Dollfuss says that Austria feels it has reached the point of intolerance regarding the activities of the National Socialist Party has caused the authorities of European countries to focus their attention on Berlin and Vienna. Dollfuss sent a note to Germany a week ago, strongly protesting interference in Austria's internal affairs. Austria has not yet responded. Those who pay attention to modern history point out that Germany is feigning deafness and muteness. What people generally worry about is that the debate on international law is playing out on the world stage, and the disarmament issue will be shelved behind the scenes.

Austrian-German Territorial Dispute Brought to the League of Nations May Not Be Effective

The Austrian Chancellor does not want to ask the League of Nations to stop the propaganda of the German National Socialist Party unless absolutely necessary, because he knows that this move will not only embarrass the League of Nations, but also exacerbate the existing resentment between Germany and Austria. Britain believes that Germany has not invaded Austrian territory, and it is doubtful whether Austria's appeal to the League of Nations is advisable or effective. Although Article 11 of the League of Nations Covenant stipulates that the League of Nations may intervene when there is a situation that endangers international relations, since the material evidence is not complete, it is feared that the impassioned speeches of international law scholars will not have a positive effect, but will only cause resentment. Austrians are now all arguing about politics, but the real difficulty lies in the provinces economically linked to Germany, which desperately want to resolve the dispute between the two countries. They are dissatisfied with Dollfuss, not without patriotism, but because trade with Germany is their only means of survival. (Reuters dispatch, 25th)

Rumors Spreading in Paris of a Secret Collaboration Between Japan and Germany

(Paris) People here generally have a skeptical attitude towards the disarmament issue. Recently, there has been a rumor that Japan has a secret agreement with Germany. According to information obtained by reporters, Japan, in view of the United States' recognition of Soviet Russia, deeply feels the future loneliness of the Japanese people. In addition, the mutual assistance between the United States and Russia in manufacturing warships and aircraft is even more frightening. Furthermore, both Germany and Japan have withdrawn from the League of Nations, but currently, the two countries have not shown any cooperation on the disarmament issue in Geneva. Recently, the Japanese Ambassador to France, Saito, stated that Japan believes that the current situation of the disarmament conference seems to be too Europeanized. If attention can be paid to the global situation in the future, Japan can definitely rejoin the discussion. The United States now adopts the same attitude towards the League of Nations disarmament issue as Japan, because the United States does not want to interfere in Europe's own political problems.

League of Nations, Upholding French Will, Formulates Three Disarmament Judgments

After recently consulting with British Prime Minister Simon and representatives from other countries such as Belgium, Romania, and Czechoslovakia, France's attitude towards Germany has become increasingly tough. France will formally propose in the League of Nations to draft a disarmament treaty and hand it over to Germany to decide whether to join the discussion. The success or failure of this conference depends solely on this. The reporter has learned that the League of Nations Executive Council has formulated three judgments as follows: (1) France will never recognize German Chancellor Hitler's proposal to increase German military strength to 300,000 and retain semi-militarized organizations. (2) The Preparatory Committee for the Disarmament Conference can proceed through diplomatic means, but the final negotiations should be held publicly in the Geneva venue. (3) In order to show its sincerity and sacrifice for the sake of the Disarmament Conference, France will submit all proposals to the Geneva Disarmament Conference. Recently, the trend of the Disarmament Conference is that Britain and France are indeed cooperating, and the United States, Japan, and Russia may all have representatives participating in the future. There will be a detailed discussion on disarmament in the Far East and all military actions. As for Germany, the outcome will definitely be slightly beneficial. (National News dispatch, 25th)

France and Germany Have Different Views on Disarmament, British Cabinet Seeks a Basis for Reconciliation

(London) The Cabinet held a meeting this afternoon, chaired by Prime Minister MacDonald, which lasted for one and a half hours. Two main issues were on the agenda: disarmament and Anglo-French commercial relations. When discussing the disarmament issue, Foreign Secretary Simon presented the report of the Cabinet's disarmament sub-committee meeting of the previous day to the cabinet members for review. The content consisted of several recommendations drafted by specialized agencies, prepared to serve as the basis for a new British mediation. It is generally believed that this proposal is based on the following considerations: (1) Reducing the importance of the "disarmament trial period" and seeking a term that can satisfy Germany's desire for equality in armaments. (2) Germany's demand for 300,000 troops can only be recognized up to 200,000. An attempt will be made to find a compromise between the two. (3) In addition, a compromise will be sought on armaments, particularly with the hope that France can specify a period and quantity for its own armament reduction, but only on the condition that Germany simultaneously fulfills its obligations. The British government intends only to submit the foregoing proposals to France and Germany through normal diplomatic channels. These proposals can be modified during the course of the negotiations. After discussing disarmament, the Cabinet then reviewed the Austrian issue. Londoners are not very willing to submit this matter to the League of Nations, because the League of Nations is currently unable to deal with this matter effectively. It would be more beneficial if the countries geographically more closely related to the matter were to deal with it. (Havas dispatch, 24th)

Contents of the Balkan Pact Encompass Five Points

Agreement on Mutual Non-Aggression

Disputes Subject to Public Judgment

Formal Establishment Expected by the End of This Month

(Paris) Yugoslavia, Turkey, and Romania are expected to sign the Balkan Pact in Athens at the end of this month. It is reported that the content of the pact includes the following points: (1) All three parties have agreed to a non-aggression pact; (2) All disputes, unless otherwise legally resolved or handled under Article 16 of the League of Nations Covenant, shall be submitted to an arbitration tribunal for judgment; (3) Each signatory country agrees to the establishment of a permanent arbitration tribunal; (4) If an arbitration tribunal cannot resolve a dispute, the case shall be sent to the Hague Peace Tribunal or the League of Nations; (5) If any signatory country is recognized by the League of Nations as having been invaded by another country, the other signatories shall rise up and provide joint assistance; (6) If the political and territorial status quo of the Balkan Peninsula countries must be maintained, the signatory countries shall assist each other. (National Telegram, 24th)

Strengthening Far East Defenses: Modernizing Singapore Naval Base

Construction Progress Must Not Be Delayed

Dilapidated Warships Rushed for Repair

British Naval Conference Held in Secrecy

(London) The Singapore Naval Conference, held yesterday aboard the flagship HMS Kent of Vice Admiral Sir Frederic Charles Dreyer, Commander-in-Chief of the British China Station, has not released a single word so far. Although the Admiralty states that this is a routine event, public opinion generally believes that this conference is the preliminary stage for making decisions of great importance to the Empire, the world, and Singapore itself. To consider the communications of the Far East, Australia, and the Pacific, the future of the naval base must be decided. The representatives attending were the Commanders-in-Chief of the British naval forces stationed in China, the East Indies, and Australia, who are responsible for protecting British interests in the western Pacific. The agenda must include modernizing Singapore into a strong naval base. Although the British government advocates a hasty policy for the Singapore naval base, there is credible reason to believe that the construction program delayed by the 1930 Imperial Conference will soon be actively continued. This project includes building a double-sized dry dock, a warship repair factory, and strengthening general defenses. Currently, British warships in the East requiring repairs must return to the home country for that purpose; if there were a well-equipped base in the Pacific, thousands of miles of travel could be avoided. (Reuters Telegram, 24th)

Dispatching Additional Warships to the Far East is Untrue

(London) The British Far East Naval Conference is currently being held in Singapore, with the HMS Kent serving as the venue. The matter is confidential, leading to rumors. Recently, a rumor from Hong Kong claimed that a large British fleet would sail to the Far East in the spring, and all Rainbow-class submarines would be transferred to China. When a Reuters reporter visited the authorities here today, they dismissed this claim as completely unfounded. (Reuters Telegram, 25th)

US House Passes Naval Appropriations Bill

Totaling Slightly Less Than 300 Million Yuan

Vinson Bill's Inclusion Unsuccessful

(Washington) The House of Representatives today passed the naval appropriations bill. The Naval Affairs Committee originally intended to incorporate the Vinson Bill, which proposed the construction of 120 new ships, into the appropriations bill as an amendment, but it ultimately failed. According to the naval appropriations bill, $284,747,000 is allocated, of which $33,619,000 is for the construction of new ships, including several aircraft carriers and four 10,000-ton cruisers. Additionally, $18,880,000 is allocated for naval aviation, including $6,131,000 for the purchase of new aircraft. However, no funds were allocated for the replacement of the Akron airship, which was lost at sea last year. (Reuters Telegram, 24th)

US Government Lifts Restrictions on Russian Imports

Duty-Free Timber Imports

Match Dumping Permitted

Ban on Russian Gold Imports to the US Relaxed

(Washington) US Treasury Secretary Morgenthau issued a statement today stating that, in order to promote US-Russian trade since the recognition of the Soviet Russian government, the US government has decided to abolish three major restrictive regulations: (1) Hereafter, the import of Russian timber and papermaking wood to the United States, all such timber being transported by US merchants who have established factories or employed labor in Russia, shall be exempt from import duties; (2) The ban on the dumping of Russian matches has also been lifted; (3) The ban on the US Mint purchasing Russian gold has also been lifted. This is the second major step to promote US-Russian trade since the arrival of the Russian Ambassador to the US, Troyanovsky. The first step was the previously announced reduction of import duties on Russian goods. (National Telegram, 24th)

Financial Problems Cause Political Turmoil in Yugoslavia

Cabinet Resigns En Masse

Belgrade The current cabinet of Sergej Jevtić has collectively resigned today. The reason is probably due to disagreements within the cabinet. On one hand, the Ministry of Finance insisted on increasing taxes, while the Minister of Education, Stankojević, reportedly made secret contacts with the opposition party without the Prime Minister's consent. When his actions were discovered, he resigned alone, thus triggering the political turmoil. (National Telegram, 24th)

Electrical Technology Decomposes Semen: Sex Can Be Determined by Humans

Successful Experiments on Rabbits

(Moscow) Professor Koltsov, Director of the Experimental Biology Institute attached to the Health Committee, announced that the institute has made a discovery of utmost importance: that researchers have been able to use electrolysis to decompose semen, separating the male and female components. Therefore, the sex of animals can now be artificially determined and adjusted. Sperm can be decomposed using artificial culture methods and applied at will. The institute has been completely successful in experiments with rabbits and will now conduct large-scale experiments in Vologda, Orenburg, and Pipooldava, regulating the sex of cattle and pigs. (TASS, 24th)

Germany Restricts Journalists: Establishes Press Courts

Newspaper Editors Can Serve as Jurors

Minor Offenses Punished with Fines, Serious Offenses with Expulsion

(Berlin) Today, Propaganda Minister Goebbels and Justice Minister Gürtner jointly issued an order tightening the restrictions on journalists. The order stipulates that each state press association shall establish a press court, and a court of appeals shall be established in Berlin. The personnel of these courts shall be specialized professionals, with no government prosecutors appearing in court. Each case shall be presided over by a judge, and publishers and editors shall be selected as jurors. Minor offenses shall be punished with fines, and serious offenses shall result in expulsion from the list of journalists of the National Socialist Party. Thereafter, the person shall no longer be allowed to practice this profession. The press court cannot handle civil, criminal, or treason cases, which shall be tried by ordinary courts. (Reuters Telegram, 24th)

Liu Xiang Meets with Gu Zhizhong, Head of the Shanghai Journalists Delegation

Liu Discusses Three Steps for Governing Sichuan

(Nanjing) Chengdu, 24th: Liu Xiang, the Pacification Commissioner of Sichuan, met with Gu Zhizhong, head of the Shanghai Journalists' Sichuan-Kang Investigation Delegation, at his office at 2 p.m. on the 22nd. He stated to Mr. Gu that although Sichuan Province cannot yet be said to be well-governed, it is progressing towards a bright future. He, himself, has three steps for governing Sichuan: pacifying bandits, post-disaster relief, and development. However, due to economic and other reasons, these three steps cannot be carried out simultaneously. Currently, all parties in Sichuan are working hard to pacify bandits, and because the people have suffered greatly from bandits, they are generally able to rise up and resist them. Therefore, the elimination of bandits is not far off. Regarding post-disaster relief, Liu hoped that everyone would change their thinking to create a new Sichuan in the future. In terms of development, Liu strongly advocated the improvement of local products and the fundamental construction of industries. Finally, he said that the current education system is not suitable and advocated the adoption of a production system in secondary education. During the implementation of these three steps, Liu hoped that the central government and the people would provide guidance and assistance. (Central News Agency Telegram, 25th)

Situation of the Panchen Lama's Arrival in Nanjing

| Whether to Return to Tibet Depends on the Central Government |

Beijing News: Due to a telegram summons from the Central Government, the Panchen Lama came south to report on the recent situation in Mongolia and Tibet. He departed from Xilin Gol League on the 17th of this month, arrived in Beiping on the 19th, and took a special train south on the 22nd. He arrived in Pukou on the afternoon of the 24th. Prior to this, the National Government received the date of departure of the Panchen Lama and notified all Yuan, ministries, commissions, and military and political organizations through the Office of the Military Council, and each sent a representative to the station to welcome him. The Gendarmerie Headquarters also sent the 6th Gendarmerie Regiment and increased security from the station to the wharf to protect him. Those who arrived at the station to welcome him included Dai Chuanxian, President of the Examination Yuan; He Yaozu, representative of Chairman Chiang; Chu Minyi, representative of President Wang; Shi Qingyang, Chairman of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission; Zhao Pilian, Vice Chairman; Huang Musong, Deputy Chief of Staff; Chen Zhuo, Director of the Police Department; and all the staff of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission and the Panchen Lama's Beijing Office, Mongolian representatives to Beijing, fellow villagers from Mongolia, Tibet, and Qinghai residing in Beijing, more than a thousand monks of the Chinese Buddhist Association, and three Tibetan representatives, including Huang Zhengqing, who arrived in Beijing from Gansu the day before. At 1:10 p.m., when the Panchen Lama's special train entered the station, the military band of the National Government and the Police Department played music, and the military police raised their guns to salute. After the train stopped, Dai Chuanxian first boarded the decorated car and presented a flower basket to express his congratulations. After the Panchen Lama accepted it, he presented each of the welcoming staff with a Hada scarf and shook hands with them to express his gratitude. Then, under the leadership of Dai Chuanxian, he got off the train and walked to the ferry. At 1:30 p.m., he crossed the river and landed on the shore. He then entered the city in a car with Dai Chuanxian and went to the Shennong Gang No. 5 Office to rest.

That afternoon at 3 p.m., the Panchen Lama met with reporters and released a statement, the main points of which were: (1) During my visit to Mongolia for several years, the Mongolians deeply felt the care of the Central Government and were able to obey its orders. Last winter, Inner Mongolia requested autonomy and held a meeting of princes in Bailingmiao. In order to convey the virtues of the Central Government, I rushed to comfort them on one hand and sent representatives to Beijing to report on the other. Therefore, the Central Government specially sent Minister Huang to Mongolia to discuss the matter in detail. After several twists and turns, this serious issue was resolved. Recently, I heard that the Mongolian representatives were dissatisfied with the autonomy plan approved by the Central Government. I have not seen the content of the plan, but I believe that the Central Government will have a way to resolve it. (2) I am deeply saddened by the passing of the Dalai Lama of Tibet. Currently, the Tibetan affairs are being handled by the regent. Politics and religion in Tibet are all as usual. I hope that the reincarnation of the Dalai Lama will appear soon to stabilize the Tibetan situation. (3) It has been more than ten years since I left Tibet. In the spring of last year, I had the intention of returning to Tibet. Initially, it was due to the Rehe Incident, then to mediate the Mongolian situation, and recently I was summoned by the Central Government, which prevented me from going. As for whether I will return to Tibet at this time, it remains to be discussed. In short, I will follow the orders of the Central Government. I have not yet decided which route to take to enter Tibet. (4) This time, I will visit the central authorities to report on everything. I have no proposals for the Fourth Plenary Session, etc.

That afternoon at 2 p.m., after the Panchen Lama arrived at the office, Shi Qingyang, He Yaozu, Huang Musong, Zhao Pilian, and others visited him successively. At 2:30 p.m., President Wang also visited the Panchen Lama's office and left after talking for about 20 minutes. Afterwards, Chairman Lin sent his Chief of Staff, Lu Chao, and Chairman Chiang also sent personnel to meet him. Upon learning of the Panchen Lama's arrival in Beijing, the Secretariat of the Central Party Headquarters sent a letter inviting him to attend the Fourth Plenary Session as an observer.

The Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission believed that the Panchen Lama had traveled a long distance to Beijing to discuss border affairs with the Central Government and had worked extremely hard. Therefore, a banquet was held at 6 p.m. that afternoon to welcome him. During the banquet, Shi Qingyang and Zhao Pilian successively delivered welcoming speeches, and the Panchen Lama gave a thank-you speech. The guests and hosts enjoyed themselves until 9 p.m.

Progress in Bandit Suppression on the West Bank of the Gan River

Xiao, Kong, and Zhang Factions All Thwarted

Yongxin Will Soon Be Recovered After Being Captured Again

Nanchang Correspondence: Since the Fujian Incident occurred last year, the Zhu-Mao pseudo-First Front Army has gathered in the Tai Ning, Jian Ning, and Ninghua area, and the military operations to suppress the communists in eastern Jiangxi have been quiet. However, the various factions on the west bank of the Gan River have been actively trying to restrain them. The bandits there were originally divided into three major factions: (1) Xiao Ke's pseudo-Eighth Army, commander of the pseudo-Gan-Xiang-Bian Military Region; (2) Kong Hechong, commander of the pseudo-Gan-E-Xiang-Bian Military Region and commander of the pseudo-Sixth Army Corps; (3) Zhang Shou, leader of the pseudo-E-Nan Military Region and leader of the pseudo-Southeast Soviet. When Xiao's bandits crossed the Gan River eastward from Wan Tai, Kong's bandits roamed from Shanggao and Gaoan through Xin'gan to the vicinity of Nanchang. Zhang's bandits attacked Yangxin and Chongtong in southern Hubei. This was because the bandits' nests were running out of supplies, and they had to leave their nests to loot. At that time, He Jian, commander of the Fourth Route Army, ordered Chen Jicheng, Liu Yinggu, Liu Jianxu, and the First, Second, and Third Columns to encircle and suppress them separately. Xiao's bandits, who crossed the Gan River, were defeated by the Wang and Luo Divisions. Gao Yongsheng's faction, which disturbed Gaoan, Fengxin, and Jingan near Nanchang, was also defeated by Tan Daoyuan and others. Gao Cun, his old nest in Wanzai, was also recovered by the Zhong Brigade. As for Zhang Shou's pseudo-1st, 7th, and 3rd and pseudo-North Jiangxi divisions, about 4,500 men with about 2,300 guns, after being driven back by Chen Jicheng and the Guo Rudong, Li Jue, and Feng Xingxian divisions, they fled to Daqiaopu, Zoumalu, and Zijing Mountain and were surrounded and severely attacked by Chen's forces, killing many bandits. Overall, the bandit forces seem to be incapable of anything.

Liu Yinggu, of the Second Column, convened a military meeting in Pingxiang to formulate strict military plans and political post-disaster plans for the central route of western Jiangxi. The Rural Cooperation Committee is organizing work relief in Pingxiang, Lianhua, and Ninggang. Yongxin County, after being captured by the bandits again, has not yet been recovered. Moreover, after Wang Dongyuan and Chen Guangzhong's divisions went south to Chongyi to take over the defense, the local forces were weakened. The defense has been redistributed and, after deployment, Yongxin will be recovered in one fell swoop. (January 22)

The Course of the Hui Tong Steamer's Burning and Destruction by Bandits

Three to Four Hundred Passengers Perished

Hankou Shipping Guild Dispatches Steamer to Recover Bodies

Hankou Dispatch: The Hui Tong small steamer, which plies between Hankou and Huangshigang, departed Huangshigang on the 20th, fully loaded with passengers and cargo heading west. That evening, while passing Baho Wharf and arriving near Yanji, it suddenly burst into flames. Hundreds of passengers perished simultaneously, and cargo losses were estimated in the tens of thousands. The steamer is owned by the Chunhe Company and is currently managed by the Jianghan Shipping Bureau. It originally sailed the Xiang River and recently began plying the Huangwu route, this being only its third voyage. After the incident, the company established the Hui Tong Steamer Disaster Temporary Relief Center at the Minquan Hotel on the 22nd, providing shelter and relief to the fifty-odd passengers rescued by the China Merchants Bureau's Jiang'an steamer. On the 23rd, the Shipping Guild dispatched the Hanfu steamer to recover bodies. In the past two months, two accidents have occurred involving Hubei Province's small steamers. On December 11th of last year, the Luan差 steamer was sunk by the Wanxiang steamer, and hundreds of new recruits were buried in the bellies of fish. Unexpectedly, not long after, the Hui Tong was burned. Three to four hundred passengers, half died by fire and half by water, making it even more cruel than the previous incident. Therefore, people in society are paying close attention. To clarify the truth, the reporter specially visited Xu Chunzhai, the manager of the company, at the Minquan Hotel. According to him, on that day, the steamer was heading west when several bandits, disguised as passengers, reached Yanji near Baho and suddenly brandished pistols, forcing the steamer to stop. While they were arguing, a fire suddenly broke out in the cabin, and the cargo of leather, oil, and cotton was ignited. Unable to be rescued, it sank. The bandits had prepared small boats in advance, used them to escape. The reason the bandits set the fire was because they had attempted a robbery in the Yanji area last week but failed. Nine members were captured by the crew and sent to the 47th Division Artillery Battalion stationed in Baho for interrogation. Two were executed, and the rest were released. Now, they have caused trouble in Yanji again, likely due to the suspicions and revenge of the bandit gang. According to another investigation, the fire was caused by cotton and oil loaded on the deck. The oil was steamed by the heat from the boiler and rolled down, catching fire. The boiler was burned and exploded, becoming uncontrollable. The steamer carried a lot of cargo and was overcrowded with passengers. Passengers filled the top of the deck. After the fire broke out, they all perished in the flames. The rest fell into the water. The so-called bandits setting the fire may be to shirk responsibility. The competent authorities for small steamers are the Navigation Administration Office of the Construction Department. Originally, small steamer inspection stations were set up in Wuxue, Tuanfeng, Baotazhou, and Hankou. However, due to the headquarters' order to reduce staff, the three stations in Wuxue, Tuanfeng, and Baotazhou were abolished, leaving only the one in Hankou. Therefore, small steamers departing from Hankou to other places can still be inspected, but those coming to Hankou from other places cannot perform their duties. The route survey and crew examinations were originally handled by the Navigation Administration Office but are no longer under its control. Before the Hui Tong incident, it had run aground several times. The mate was newly replaced, and the route survey and crew examinations may also have been negligent. The company's greed for loading more goods was the source of the disaster. The authorities have decided to deal with this strictly. (24th)

Songjiang

Murderer Escorted to Suzhou for Appeal

The case of the murder of the owner Xi Weiquan and his wife of the Xiyongda Rice Store on Huayang Bridge, involving the arrest of the principal offender Shen Ahe, as well as the deceased's brother Xi Weisheng, concubine Song Xiaomei, and unrelated robbers Shen Abing and Wu Zixiang, has been thoroughly investigated by the Songjiang County Court. Xi Weisheng, Song Xiaomei, and Shen Ahe were sentenced to death for premeditated murder. The robbers Shen Abing and Wu Zixiang were each sentenced to fifteen years of imprisonment. The convicts, being dissatisfied with the verdicts, filed appeals with the Jiangsu High Court within the statutory period. The High Court approved the appeals and scheduled a hearing for the 27th of this month. The County Court dispatched bailiffs Tao Jinhe and Li Fuyuan, along with four police officers, all fully armed, to escort the five convicts from the detention center. They were transported to Suzhou by car this morning (25th) to await trial. It is reported that Xi Weisheng and Song Xiaomei have hired lawyers Zhang Yipeng and Lu Longxiang to defend them at the time.

Suzhou

Octogenarian Marries

At the Da Hongyun Auditorium on Daoqian Street inside Xumen, an eighty-year-old man recently married a twenty-eight-year-old virgin, causing a sensation. Tea houses and taverns spread the news as a good story. It is now known that the man's name is Shen Hongxi, and he is seventy-nine years old. He is from Qingpu and owns 3,000 mu of fertile land and 300,000 yuan in cash. He has two sons, one doing business in the area and one working in the banking industry in Shanghai. His eldest daughter-in-law is also fifty years old. However, his wife passed away early, so he handed over the family property to his sons and daughters-in-law to manage, and built another house to live with a widowed woman he had living with him. The bride's surname is Xu, and she lives in Cao Hu Xu Lane in Suzhou. She is a cousin of Shi Junqing, the current chairman of the Wuxian Chamber of Commerce. The root of this matter is that the old man had an affair with a woman he had hired, but the eldest daughter-in-law rebuked and drove the woman away. The old man was angry and took back half of his family property, vowing to marry one wife and one concubine for his amusement. It is heard that the choice of the concubine is being sought and negotiated.
