Money Industry Leader Qin Runqing Publishes Opinions on Currency Revolution

Recent Cash Surplus Does Not Imply Money Shortage

Issuing Non-Convertible Currency Will Lead to a Dead End

The "Ability Standard" System Is Extremely Difficult to Implement in Our Country

The Xin Sheng News Agency reports: Qin Runqing, Chairman of the Shanghai Money Industry Association, recently replied to a letter from Legislative Yuan member Jiao Yitang, stating: "Mr. Yitang, upon returning from Ningbo, I received your letter. I deeply admire your plan for a currency revolution to save the nation. However, in my humble opinion, the theory of the 'ability standard system' is somewhat fanciful and can only serve as material for scholars to discuss. It seems difficult to implement in the immediate future. Take our country as an example. From exchanging cloth for silk to casting currency and establishing a monetary system, people have been accustomed to using coins for thousands of years. Only recently has paper money become popular, but it is always based on full cash reserves. If a company suspends convertibility, panic ensues. Ignoring distant events,

The Scars of Wuhan Have Not Yet Healed. The Wuhan cash concentration incident occurred seven years ago, and Hubei's finances have not yet recovered to their former state. The plight of bill holders at that time is still fresh in my mind. If the limited amount of non-convertible paper money caused such severe harm in one area, then the unlimited issuance of substitute vouchers planned by Mr. Liu would almost certainly drive the people of the country into destitution. Recently, there have been widespread reports of a cash surplus in the country, and I have not heard of a money shortage. If it is said that the countryside is poor, this is fundamentally due to natural disasters and man-made calamities, leading to rural bankruptcy. Even if Mr. Liu's plan is implemented, those who rely on claiming the substitute vouchers would only be the wealthy. The common people in the countryside have no possessions, and even finding enough to eat is difficult. Where would they get the capital to exchange for vouchers? Moreover, the result of excessive issuance of substitute vouchers would inevitably lead to soaring prices. Even if wages could be increased, the rate of increase would be difficult to keep up. The consequences would be that farmers and workers throughout the country would be driven to desperation and take desperate risks. Although the world is evolving daily, the term 'paper standard' remains an ominous term in economics.

Germany's Experience Serves as a Warning. After the Great War, Germany lost battles and territory, and owed hundreds of millions in reparations, leaving its finances in dire straits. The Minister of Agriculture was at a loss.

They had no choice but to use the printing press in place of the mint, with bundles of paper money being taken to the market to exchange for a loaf of bread. There were many people in the country at the time who had lived there. The state of national commotion, with no one able to live in peace, is not

difficult to recall. If Mr. Liu's words were true, then Germany would have implemented it long ago and should have wiped away the shame of defeat and become invincible. Why, then, did they immediately reform the currency system and destroy the old, excessively issued paper money as soon as they had a way out, fearing that they would not be able to do so completely? Furthermore, although the idea of ​​currency inflation is advocated by the United States, the United States is suffering from overproduction, while my country is suffering from underproduction. The situations are completely opposite, so how can we force a fit? Moreover, the United States' currency inflation plan also focuses on gradual progress. Therefore, even though it is known as the "Gold Dollar Kingdom," it has hesitated to issue a plan for some non-convertible bonds, and has not yet implemented it. At most, it will only reduce the gold dollar component.

Technocracy. This is a term in "technical politics," originally coined by a veteran of that country. It was not initially valued by scholars. Only in recent years, with the New World shrouded in depression and unable to recover, did Americans, in their resentment, suddenly hear of the novelty of the theory and spared no effort to spread it, treating it as a rare commodity. By the time President Roosevelt took office, the situation had been renewed, and the project had gradually succeeded. Thus, the term "technocracy" faded away like a flash in the pan and is about to become a historical term. Why do people treat it like worn-out shoes, while we still cherish it like a precious treasure, considering it to be on the same path?

Currency Needs Are Inherently Small. To say that the average amount of silver coins in the hands of people throughout the country is less than three yuan, and to regard this as evidence of chaos and money shortage, is not an accurate argument. We do not need to look back to the rule of Emperors Yao and Shun. Even in the middle of the Qing Dynasty, the country was at peace. The wealth of the country at that time was far beyond what we can imagine today. How much currency did the people of the whole country have in their hands at that time? Even Mexican silver coins from that time can still be seen in the coastal provinces. Even the total value of copper coins is less than one-tenth of today's copper coins. It can be seen that the amount of currency has nothing to do with national strength. It all depends on the evolution of the people's living standards for increase or decrease. For example, the cost of living in the United States is extremely high, and ordinary wages cannot be less than five or six yuan per day. Therefore, the amount of currency needed is naturally large, and the amount of currency in the hands of each person is also large. The same applies to the United Kingdom, Germany, France, and Japan. As for our country, the cost of living is low. A daily wage of two or three yuan is only seen in major trading ports, and a family of seven farmers and workers can live comfortably on tens of dollars a year. Since the need for currency is small, the amount in hand cannot be compared with that of the United Kingdom and the United States. If we add inflation, it is no different from feeding an adult's portion to a child's stomach, which will inevitably cause bloating and premature death. In short, even the "ability standard system" is something that the Soviet Union is still hesitant to implement. To say that it can achieve long-term stability and prosperity in our country, I am unlearned and cannot fathom its profoundness. I have taken the liberty of answering your questions and offer my humble opinions. I hope you will forgive my candor and remain in good health.

Joint Chamber of Commerce Submits to Zhejiang Finance Department Requesting Exemption from Business Tax for Exhibition Hall

The Shanghai Machinery-Made National Products Factory Joint Association has submitted a request to the Zhejiang Provincial Finance Department, requesting that the Hangzhou National Products Exhibition Hall, which has recently been forced to pay business tax by the Zhejiang Provincial Business Tax Bureau, be exempted from taxation in accordance with regulations. The original document is transcribed below:

Letter to the Joint Chamber of Commerce: The Hangzhou National Products Exhibition Hall writes to the Joint Chamber of Commerce, stating: "The National Products Exhibition Hall is a part of the entire National Products Exhibition Hall. Merchants participate in business and are in a position to assist the government in promoting national products. According to the principles of the Business Tax Law, government-run enterprises are not subject to taxation. However, exhibition hall shops are subject to restrictions everywhere and are not comparable to shops that are purely for profit. According to the law, there is no possibility of taxation. The Capital National Products Exhibition Hall, the Shanghai Commodities Exhibition Hall, and the National Products Exhibition Halls in Hebei, Hunan, and other provinces all exempt business tax for shops in their attached business areas. The original intention is very clear, and the method is very appropriate. However, the Zhejiang National Products Exhibition Hall is also under the rule of the National Government. Repeated requests have been made to exempt the business tax of the shopping mall, but they have never been approved. The business nature is the same, so how can the government's treatment be different? The total amount of business tax to be levied in the entire venue is only more than 1,000 yuan. The sluggish business of the shopping mall is on the verge of collapse. If it is exempted, it will not have any impact on the overall tax revenue of Zhejiang Province, but it will have endless benefits for the continuation of the life of national products. Recently, the Business Tax Bureau has been urging the shopping mall to pay taxes, and the entire venue is in a state of anxiety and panic. It is generally believed that the business of the shopping mall is precarious, and the government does not maintain or rescue it. How can it be willing to rob Peter to pay Paul? It is inappropriate both legally and emotionally. It is decided to petition the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Finance again and send telegrams to both the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, requesting that the tax exemption be achieved. Otherwise, any sacrifice will be made. It is highly expected and grateful to be able to appeal to your association to lead the national products and establish a reputation."

Submission to the Zhejiang Provincial Government: The Joint Chamber of Commerce submits to the Zhejiang Provincial Finance Department, stating: "The submission is for the matter of submission. It is reported that a public letter from the Shopping Mall Joint Association attached to the Zhejiang Provincial National Products Exhibition Hall stated, (omitted)... The meeting found that all undertakings promoted and encouraged by the government are exempt from various donations and taxes. Moreover, the National Products Exhibition Hall is a government-run enterprise and is not subject to taxation. How can we bear to destroy the business of the sluggish shopping mall with this mere tax, violating the original purpose of government promotion? Thinking about it quietly, the Business Tax Bureau will never have such a cruel heart. Therefore, we specially appeal to your department to examine and approve the order to the Business Tax Bureau to exempt the shopping mall from business tax, so as to promote and benefit national products. This is for the public good."

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Tonghua Steamer Damaged in Collision

Due to Beikang Steamer Chasing Yuehang in the Baihe River

The Tonghua steamer originally sailed the Haizhou Laoyao route. Recently, due to the congestion of combined transportation goods, it was reassigned to a larger ship for navigation. In the North China route, it is currently the winter ice age. The Tonghua has a shallow draft due to its load, so it changed its route to Tianjin. Jiang Changqing, the owner of the Tunan ship, was transferred to Tonghua to familiarize himself with the ship. After arriving in Tianjin and unloading the cargo, Tonghua left Tianjin on the 19th of this month to return to Shanghai. Unexpectedly, after sailing out of the Baihe River, the Beikang steamer of the Northern Company collided with the Tonghua's hull from behind while traveling forward. This was truly beyond the bounds of reasonable collision at sea.

Report on the Cause: The Tonghua steamer's owner, Jiang Changqing, reported the truth about the collision to the head office, stating: "The Tonghua steamer sailed from Tianjin to the Baihe River on the 19th of this month at 11:18 a.m. It is currently the ice age, and the water level is shallower than usual. While the Tonghua was sailing forward, the Beikang steamer of the Northern Shipping Company also set sail from Tianjin and wanted to overtake the Tonghua from behind. The ship suddenly opened up a special fast speed and rushed forward. When it was close to the Tonghua and about to pass, the Beikang hit the Tonghua's outer hull steel plate and other parts. Fortunately, the Tonghua dodged quickly and did not cause a tragic accident."

Demand for Compensation: After receiving the report from Captain Jiang and sending personnel to the Tonghua steamer to inspect the damage, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company sent a letter to the Northern Company, stating that the Beikang steamer was chasing the ship ahead on the same route in the Baihe River during the shallow water ice age, increasing its speed, making it impossible for the Tonghua to prevent or avoid the collision, which was a violation of navigation regulations and caused the accident. All repair losses to the Tonghua steamer caused by the Beikang collision should be the full responsibility of the Beikang steamer. While sending a letter, the company also had the damaged parts repaired so that it could sail to Nanhua.

Joint Chamber of Commerce Requests Enactment of Regulations to Punish Traitorous Merchants

Severely Punish Those Who Collude With Foreigners to Deceive Society

Regulations on Country of Origin Labeling Should Be Implemented Early

The Xin Sheng News Agency reports: The Shanghai Machinery-Made National Products Factory Joint Association recently received a report from the Electrical Manufacturing Industry Association regarding the discovery of "headless" counterfeit light bulbs and requested that measures be taken to stop them. The association specially submitted a document to the Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating: "The submission is for the matter of 'headless' light bulbs being imported by taking advantage of loopholes, requesting that they be taxed as finished products and that regulations to punish traitorous merchants be swiftly enacted to achieve practical results.' It is found that the dumping of Japanese goods in the domestic market is becoming more and more serious. Our country is the first to bear the brunt, and industry and commerce are suffering the most. The association submitted a document to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce on February 12 of last year, clearly stating the situation of Japanese goods being dumped and requesting that Japanese light bulbs be taxed as dumping goods. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce issued a secret telegram No. 16348, ordering the Committee for the Review of Dumped Goods to deliberate and respond, based on which to review and handle the matter. Unexpectedly, the Japanese are cunning. Before our country has implemented the collection of dumping tax on Japanese light bulbs, they have changed their methods and used their cunning to import light bulbs without copper heads, pretending to be raw materials, reducing costs, and encroaching on the market. From this, it can be inferred that there are rumors that Japanese goods are being transported and unloaded in the leased territories within their sphere of influence, colluding with traitorous merchants, selling under fake brands, and evading customs duties. Such facts have traces to be found, and the harm is not limited to the light bulb industry. In the humble opinion of the association, in addition to ordering all customs offices to tax light bulbs without copper heads as finished products or semi-finished products and strictly ordering secret investigations into smuggling and tax evasion, the regulations on country of origin labeling should be implemented early. At the same time, regulations to punish traitorous merchants should be enacted separately. Any Chinese merchant who colludes with foreign merchants to engage in various improper transactions, disrupts the domestic market, directly affects national tax revenue, endangers national products, indirectly deceives society, and weakens national strength should be severely punished if there is concrete evidence. In this way, even if the country's military force is not enough to resist strong neighbors, punishing traitorous merchants will not be difficult. Punishing one will serve as a warning to others, and we will achieve the practical effect of drawing firewood from under the cauldron. Whether it is appropriate, the letter from the Electrical Manufacturing Industry Association is hereby submitted to your department for examination and implementation. Both national treasury revenue and the future of national products will benefit from this. We earnestly submit this with respect." At the same time, the association also submitted a request to the National Tariff Committee to levy tax on headless light bulbs at the rate of finished products.

Meeting Minutes of the Chinese Cigarette Factory Association

The Advantages and Disadvantages of Unequal Tax Revenue Between Chinese and Foreign Companies

Guo Wen News Agency reports: Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 p.m., the Shanghai Chinese Cigarette Factory Association held a supplementary general meeting of members at the Central Western Restaurant auditorium on Four Horse Road. A total of 28 members attended, four of whom were representatives without formal letters, so the meeting was changed to a discussion meeting. The temporary chairman, Wu Tingsheng, opened the meeting as usual. First, the chairman reported on the process of the Ministry of Finance agreeing to allocate 300,000 yuan for the development of the tobacco industry, briefly stating that Chinese merchants have weak capital and are often subjected to economic oppression by foreign merchants, so they requested the government to allocate 500,000 yuan from tax revenue to develop their businesses. Later, Mr. Wu and Mr. Shen Bao represented the association in petitioning, and Minister of Finance Kong agreed to allocate 300,000 yuan. Then, the issue of safekeeping was discussed. Since this fund is a subsidy for Chinese merchants, it should naturally be kept by Chinese merchants. Next, Mr. Huang Ziping gave a speech on how the government's change in tax collection methods has affected business, briefly stating that according to the Unified Tax Gazette and the Tax Gazette, when the three-level tax was implemented, British-American Tobacco Company sold 30,472 boxes per month, totaling 2,417,403,822 yuan, while Chinese merchants sold 68,422 boxes, totaling 2,006,252,647 yuan. Since the change to the two-level tax, British-American Tobacco Company has sold 48,808 boxes per month, totaling 2,726,392,522 yuan, while Chinese merchants have sold 44,323 boxes, totaling 2,554,466,996 yuan. From this, it can be seen that since the change to the two-level tax, Chinese merchants have sold 24,009 boxes less, which is 24,099 fewer boxes of cigarettes, but the tax has increased by 548,214,340 yuan, causing foreign merchants to sell 18,336 more boxes, which is 18,336 more boxes of cigarettes, but the tax revenue has only increased by 308,988,700 yuan. The disadvantage of the two-level tax to Chinese merchants is evident, and we should find ways to improve it. Moreover, each time the tax is changed, Chinese merchants sell fewer packages of cigarettes. A table is shown below:

Tax Level Anhui (Susong) Hubei (Huanggang) Zhejiang (Xinchang) Henan (Champion) Hubei (Guangshui) Henan (Junzhou) Total Annual Sales

Seven Level 12,000 Packages 80,000 Packages 50,000 Packages 30,000 Packages 10,000 Packages 50,000 Packages 390,000 Packages

Three Level 90,000 Packages 50,000 Packages 40,000 Packages 20,000 Packages 30,000 Packages 265,000 Packages

Two Level 40,000 Packages 30,000 Packages 15,000 Packages 15,000 Packages 115,000 Packages

Therefore, each time the tax rules are changed, sales decrease. After Mr. Huang's report, the meeting was changed to the next discussion due to insufficient attendance.

After the meeting, the reporter met with Mr. Huang to discuss the unequal phenomenon of cigarette tax between Chinese and foreign companies. According to him, Chinese merchants have small capital and can only engage in business. The average capital for each box of low-grade cigarettes is 65 yuan, but the current tax is 80 yuan. This tax is calculated as a percentage, which is 120 percent on a value of 100. Foreign merchants have large capital and mostly deal in high-grade cigarettes. The average capital for each box is 220 yuan, but the tax is 80 yuan, which is only 36 percent. We cannot accept this unequal treatment. However, we are not resisting taxation. According to my opinion, whether it is Chinese or foreign merchants, if the tax is 100 percent on a value of 100, the government can increase tax revenue by 60 million yuan per year.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Requests Prompt Dredging of the Suzhou Creek

And Clearing of Stranded Vessels

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce submitted a report to the Municipal Government yesterday, stating: "The submission is for a factual petition. On the 22nd of this month, the Shanghai Inland River Steamer Industry Association, a member of the association, stated in a letter that 'the Suzhou Creek extends west to Xiepu and east to Su and Chang, and is a vital passage for inland river navigation. In recent years, due to the increasing silting, when the tide recedes, the number of ships traveling to and from is too large, and they are all stranded on the silt, unable to sail. Although the tide has risen greatly recently, as the end of the old year is approaching, the goods from the countryside coming to Shanghai for sale are extremely crowded, and the American wheat ordered by the flour mills is also being imported one after another, and are being transported to the mills for use. These ships are very large, resulting in congestion. The regular ships from Suzhou and Wuxi belonging to our companies are therefore blocked in the area of ​​Sampan Factory Bridge and Yidaikou, unable to approach the wharf. They have been congested since the 11th of this month, and have been suspended for eight days. Although the past two days have been high tides, the ships jammed still could not be cleared completely. In the winter season of low tides and small tides, if we do not request the authorities to take measures to provide relief, not only will water traffic be completely cut off, but also the suspension of our company's ships will result in great losses to our business. In desperation, we request your association to promptly forward the matter to the authorities and take measures to clear the congestion in order to maintain business and facilitate navigation.' Based on this, the association sent personnel to conduct an on-site investigation, and verified that the facts were completely consistent with the above. It was also found that ship congestion is of great importance to water security. If measures are not taken quickly to clear the congestion, not only will the steamer industry be affected, but all industries will suffer its impact, and water security will also be greatly disrupted. Based on the above situation, we urgently prepare a letter and forward it to your association, requesting you to promptly forward it to the Public Security Bureau of the Municipal Government, and take measures to provide relief in order to maintain security and facilitate transportation." Based on this, the Suzhou Creek is the only important waterway for inland river navigation. Recently, due to increasing silting, when the river tide recedes, many ships traveling to and from are stranded in the area of Sampan Factory Bridge and Yidaikou, which not only hinders

Communication also accumulates goods, making it necessary to dredge them as soon as possible. In accordance with the facts, we hereby submit a request, asking your government to examine and approve it, and order the competent bureau to estimate the work and start dredging immediately. At the same time, order the Public Security Bureau to order the water patrol team to find ways to clear the ships that accumulate every day, so as to maintain water security and benefit travelers. This is for the public good. Respectfully submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Government."

Request for Private Airlines to Participate in Intermodal Transport Submitted for Review and Approval

Can Be Submitted to the Ministry in One Week

The Implementation Period for Participation Is Not Far Away

The Municipal Aviation Association Is Actively Handling the Matter

Private shipping companies' participation in water-land intermodal transport has been decided by the Ministry of Communications and the Ministry of Railways. The shipping bureaus must first open their ships, wharves, routes, etc., and report them to the ministry, and then the ministry will review and approve them. The Shipping Association is actively preparing for this matter. The latest news is checked as follows:

Proposed Rush: Since the Municipal Shipping Association has been fighting for the participation of private shipping companies in intermodal transportation, it is now gradually showing signs of success. However, in view of the fact that China Merchants Group has recently been actively conducting intermodal transportation matters with the Ministry of Railways on routes other than the Longhai Railway, and private companies have not yet achieved their participation goal, the Municipal Shipping Association specially convened representatives of shipping companies on the 11th of this month to discuss urgent measures. As a result, it was decided that the first step would be to submit all private airlines to the ministry and request that they be included in intermodal transportation.

Submission Format: The Municipal Shipping Association specially drafted a form and distributed it to private shipping companies, ordering them to fill it out as soon as possible so that they could be submitted to the ministry for review. The submission format is as follows: The submitter is a private shipping company. Now, I would like to participate in water-land intermodal transportation. I hereby list the items that should be opened for your review. They are: (1) Company name, (2) Location of the head office and branches, (3) All ships, listed by ship name, total tonnage, and route, (4) Wharf police station, (5) Approval to allow XX ship to regularly travel on XX route and conduct intermodal transportation with XX railway, (6) Willing to join the private-state-run water-land intermodal transportation office and share its expenses in proportion to the tonnage of goods transported. This submission is respectfully submitted to XX Department. The submitter's name and the person in charge's name.

Urgent Filling and Reporting: The Municipal Shipping Association is aware that many companies have filled in and submitted the forms according to the table, but there are still those who have not filled them in. Beiyin urgently submitted the forms to the ministry, so it issued an urgent notice to the shipping companies, stating: "In view of the fact that the participation in water-land intermodal transportation was previously decided by the Executive Committee, the submission format was sent to the companies for filling in as early as the 11th of this month. Now that it has been a long time, many members have filled in the submission and sent it to the association, and have urged the association to forward it to the ministry as soon as possible. There are still some who have not filled it in. Now that China Merchants Group is working hard to advance intermodal transportation on various routes, private airlines must not miss the opportunity again. Please make sure that your company submits the submission before the 31st of this month, otherwise it will be regarded as unwilling to join intermodal transportation. The Municipal Shipping Association will forward the ships' tonnage, routes, warehouses, wharves, etc., of the private airline companies that have been filled in and submitted to the Ministry of Communications and the Ministry of Railways for review and approval. After being approved to participate in intermodal transportation, the companies will form a general agency to undertake intermodal transportation to manage the matter. It is estimated that the submission can be forwarded to the ministry for review in one week."

Hydrographic Survey Bureau Notifies Shipping

West Zhou Buoy Moves

The Central News Agency reports that the Hydrographic Survey Bureau has moved the position of the "West Zhou" buoy in the Yangtze River estuary on January 24. Yesterday, it issued a notice to ships, informing various shipping bureaus to pay attention. Its new position is 1.9 nautical miles from the "West Zhou" marker due north at 33 degrees, or approximately 120 degrees 5 minutes east longitude and 31 degrees 47 minutes north latitude. Also, due to the discovery of a sunken ship near Shantou on the southeast coast and southeast of Nan'ao Island, it is also

notifying the shipping industry to pay attention. Its position is on the semi-tidal reef southeast of Nan'ao Island, 146.5 degrees due north from the top of Yandun Mountain, 1.5 nautical miles away, or approximately 117 degrees 8 minutes east longitude and 23 degrees 22 minutes north latitude. There is a sunken ship, and its hull and one mast are exposed 30 feet above the water at low tide.

Work Report of the Legal Department of the Public Works Bureau for the Previous Year

The head of the Legal Department of the Public Works Bureau of the Public Concession's work report for 1933 stated that the agreement with the courts in the concession was extended on February 8 of that year. Since the establishment of the court three years ago, there have been several difficulties and differences of opinion in the work, but there have been no serious disagreements. The judges and the representatives of the Public Works Bureau are friendly and mutually respectful. Therefore, all differences of opinion have been resolved satisfactorily. During the period of 1933, the criminal section of the court, with the assistance of the Public Works Bureau, was very smooth. There were as many as 33,134 minor and major criminal cases this year, and by the end of the year, only 42 cases remained unresolved, excluding appeals. An average of 89 cases were handled per day, and the number of cases unresolved in one year was less than half a day's work. This speed is rare in other courts. The ratio of the number of sentences to the number of prosecutions this year was 92.5%, which is a high score and shows the effectiveness of the prosecution and the hard work of the police department's investigation and preparation work.

It is estimated that the number of people prosecuted in the First Special District Court and the Jiangsu High Court this year was 128,889 (101,570 in 1932). Among them, 94,625 people committed minor offenses attached to the law and did not appear in court. The bail was confiscated according to regulations. In 1,130 cases, the charges were withdrawn due to insufficient evidence. In addition, a total of 33,134 minor and major criminal cases were concluded (26,217 in the previous year), of which 30,676 people were found guilty and sentenced, and 2,458 people were acquitted. The ratio of those sentenced to the number of prosecutions was 92.5%. Since the establishment of the two laws on April 1, 1930, the total average of this ratio has been 92.3%.

In addition to the above, there were also 2,215 private criminal cases, 6,303 cases of violations prosecuted by the health and public affairs departments (3,181 cases in the previous year), and 7,973 cases of violations prosecuted by the motor vehicle section (5,591 cases in the previous year).

Of the appeals filed by the Public Works Bureau, there were 25 this year. In addition, there were 11 appeals from the previous year that were not concluded, for a total of 36. Of the 30 appeals that were tried and concluded, 11 were dismissed, 3 were remanded for retrial, and 16 were given heavier sentences. At the end of the year, there were 6 unresolved appeals, including 2 in the Supreme Court and 4 in the High Court.

Of the 655 appeals filed by the defendants, adding the 119 cases not concluded the previous year, there were a total of 774 cases. Among them, 700 cases were tried and concluded. As a result, 452 were dismissed, 40 were withdrawn, 46 were acquitted, 116 had their sentences reduced, 16 had their sentences increased, 25 were remanded for retrial, 2 were not accepted, 1 was dismissed, and 2 cases were transferred to the city court for trial due to incorrect jurisdiction. There were 74 appeals not concluded at the end of the year, including 59 in the Supreme Court, 14 in the High Court, and 1 in the District Court.

Of the "transferred cases" filed by government offices outside the concession, there were 185 cases involving 352 people. Among them, the evidence was established for 312 people, and they were ordered to be transferred. 14 people were released due to insufficient evidence. 15 people were released on bail pending trial. 1 person was sent to the Japanese authorities. 10 people had their original cases withdrawn.

Unresolved cases: As of December 31, 1933, there were 42 cases in the local and high courts, plus 80 unresolved appeals, for a total of 122 cases. In addition, there were 8 cases where the defendant was in temporary custody.

Probation cases: There were 515 new cases where imprisonment was suspended, and 22 cases where probation was granted on appeal. 91,232 criminal documents were served by the police department, and 7,168

documents were served by judicial police. A total of 117,311 civil documents were served by bailiffs.

Ministry of Industry Official Repeatedly Receives Extortion Letters

Received Five Letters in Succession Demanding $5,000

Police Dispatch Detectives to Stake Out and Arrest Criminals

He Weikangpu, styled Zejin, a senior official in the Ministry of Industry, residing at No. 48, Fukang Lane, Xinza Road,

suddenly received a threatening letter from a criminal gang on October 5 last year, containing fierce words and intending to extort $5,000. It also specified a time and place to negotiate payment. After receiving the letter, Ji ignored it. Unexpectedly, the criminal gang sent a letter every two days. By this month, Ji had received five letters in succession, and also made telephone inquiries from time to time. Ji then prepared a reply, stating, "I am not a wealthy family, please do not send any more letters," and handed it over to rickshaw driver Lu San to deliver to the place specified by the criminal gang. In order to avoid trouble, Ji

moved to the Chinese district, No. 2, Lane 2, Xin Village, Yanan Road and Connaught Road, a few days ago. Unexpectedly, the criminal gang was well-informed, and on the 23rd of this month,

Ji received another threatening letter, demanding $5,000 and ordering that the money be sent to the wastepaper basket on the bamboo fence behind the public toilet on Changping Road between 9:00 and 10:00 a.m. on the 24th. If he did not comply, danger would ensue. At this point, Ji had no choice but to report the letter to the chief inspector's office of the General Police Station, which informed the Gordon Road Police Station in charge. The police chief immediately ordered detectives to investigate the matter that night. They saw a bamboo

fence

without a wastepaper basket. Until yesterday morning, Chinese detectives Zhu

Hanbo and Cai Liu, Western detective Moore, and Chinese detective Zhao Qingkui, as well as private detectives, all disguised themselves at 8:30 a.m., some as rickshaw pullers with rickshaws in hand, some as vendors with shoulder poles, and secretly waited near the toilet. They saw a wastepaper basket hanging on the bamboo fence. Ji Kangpu sent rickshaw driver Lu San as a representative to put a paper package disguised as $5,000 in banknotes into

the wastepaper basket. Until 11:00,

A Criminal Gang Appears: Xu Alin from Tongzhou, Chen Asan from Chongming, and Zhu Zhangming from Pudong. Xu rode a bicycle to the destination on Changping Road and handed the bicycle over to Zhu for safekeeping. Xu and Chen walked to the back of the toilet and carefully checked the wastepaper basket. Seeing that the paper package was there, Chen pretended to urinate, and Xu touched the paper package and hid it on his person. At that time, the detectives who had been waiting for a long time had witnessed the actions of these people. At this point, they gave a secret signal, and the ambush detectives came out together and arrested Xu and the other two, along with the paper package and bicycle, and took them to the police station. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Criminal Court No. 8 of the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Jiang Baolian, in addition to prosecuting the three defendants under Article 370 of the Criminal Code for

extortion and attempted fraud, and Article 3 of the Provisional Regulations for the Punishment of Bandits, also stated the circumstances of the case. He said that the victim, Ji Kangpu, had moved to the Chinese district a few days ago, but the criminal gang had learned of Ji's address, and Ji had received a call from the criminal gang yesterday morning, which was quite surprising, because Ji had only moved recently, and the phone was newly installed, and Ji's name and address were not on the phone book. It was strange how the criminal gang had learned of it, so the prosecution requested a postponement of the case for investigation. Then, according to the victim, Ji Kangpu, he stated the circumstances of receiving the letters. According to the witness Lu San, after he was ordered to put the paper package into the wastepaper basket yesterday morning, at about 11:00, the defendant Chen Asan came and asked me if I was

sent from the west (because Ji lived in western Shanghai). I replied yes, and asked if I had brought the money. I replied yes. Xu Alin then took the paper package from the wastepaper basket and hid it on his person before being arrested by the detectives. The defendant Zhu Zhangming was holding the bicycle and standing by the side of the road, etc. Questioned, the defendant Xu Alin confessed that the matter was entirely done by Qian Afu, who was at large. Because I came to Shanghai from Suzhou on the second day of the lunar month and met Qian behind Carter Road and Baker Road, I was invited to Qian's house on Matt Hirst Road. Qian suddenly said that he had a classmate who was quite wealthy, and he had written a letter instructing me and Chen Asan to go and get the money. On the 23rd night, Qian led us to Changping Road to identify the address, and I went home to sleep. Qian hung up the wastepaper basket, and yesterday morning I went to Qian's house. A friend of Qian's, someone A, arrived on a bicycle, so I switched to riding it and went to Changping Road with Chen Asan. I saw Zhu Zhangming passing by and asked Zhu to take care of the bicycle temporarily, and took the paper package and was arrested. Qian and others were standing in the nearby fields, etc. Chen Asan confessed to going with Xu to get the money, but said he did not know about the threatening letters. Zhu Zhangming's confession was evasive. Judge Wu Tingqi verified the confession and ordered the defendants to be detained for another seven days for questioning.

French Concession Levies New Medical Examination Fee for Prostitutes

Three Yuan Per Prostitute Per Month to Be Borne by Brothels

The French Consul General in Shanghai, in order to rectify the issue of brothels in the concession keeping prostitutes with infectious diseases, amended Article 7 of the Public Works Bureau's regulations on the management of brothels and promulgated it for implementation. The method is to order each brothel to be subject to medical examination by a doctor, and to be examined every half month thereafter. Gang Fight Between Robbers and Police in the Countryside of Houjia Lane, Haige Road

Both Sides Battled on Barren Land for a Long Time

A Chinese Policeman Shot and Wounded in the Arm Still Fought Back

|Two Wounded Robbers Detained in Hospital One After Another|

At around 2:00 a.m. yesterday morning, a gunfight between robbers and police occurred at the intersection of Haige Road, Houjia Lane, the Chinese district, the Public Concession, and the French Concession. As a result, one robber was captured on the spot, one robber was detained in the hospital, one robber escaped, and one Chinese policeman was shot and wounded. The details are recorded as follows:

Brothers Diligently and Frugally Manage Their Household: Houjia Lane (i.e., Third Embankment Lane 5) opposite the Chinese Funeral Parlor on Haige Road in western Shanghai is located at the intersection of the Chinese and Concession districts. It is a remote and sparsely populated area with only a dozen villagers living in separate households. Wang Maozi and Wang Shudong are brothers who work as farmers. They are diligent and frugal in managing their household. Although the property inherited from their ancestors is very small, they can make ends meet by saving on expenses. In recent years, they have accumulated some savings. At the same time, because of the busy farming, the two brothers were unable to take care of everything, so they hired a farm worker to help. Unexpectedly, they were coveted by bandits.

Bandits Suddenly Arrived in the Middle of the Night: At around 1:00 a.m. yesterday morning, when the Wang brothers and the farm worker Xiao Di were all asleep, several bandits suddenly came to the outside of the Wang brothers' house and pried open the door. One of the bandits used a flashlight to shine inward to scout. At that time, the farm worker Xiao Di happened to wake up to go to the toilet. The bandits heard the sound and were very happy. They hid on both sides of the door and waited for Xiao Di to come out. They rushed up together, forbade him to make a sound, and forced him to lead them inside to search each room. The Maozi brothers were also awakened, and because they could not resist, they let them do as they pleased. The bandits were very disappointed that the Wang brothers had nothing of value, so they quickly rolled up some better clothes and fled outside.

Calling for Help from All Sides: After the bandits walked out of the door, the Wang brothers and the farm worker Xiao Di shouted to catch the robbers. At the same time, the neighbors also heard the alarm and responded. The bandits saw that things were not going well and planned to flee west. At that time, police officers No. 2480 and No. 3002 from the Jing'an Temple Police Station happened to be passing by. They heard the alarm and saw black shadows running wildly in front of them. They knew that they were not good people, so they used flashlights to investigate and chased after them. The bandits saw the police officers

chasing closely behind and opened fire backwards in desperation.

Chinese Policeman Shot and Wounded: Therefore, the two police officers also returned fire. The two sides engaged in a fierce battle on this barren land for a long time. Chinese police officer No. 3002 was shot in the right arm, but he did not flinch and continued to fight. Before long, two black shadows fell to the ground, and at the same time, the bandits' gunshots stopped. The police officers knew that they had been injured, so they rushed forward to arrest them, but they had already disappeared. It turned out that the bandits had escaped. Police officer No. 2480 quickly sent the injured police officer No. 3002 to the police hospital for treatment and reported to the police station to pursue the escaped wounded bandits.

Wounded Robber Voluntarily Went to the Hospital: After receiving the report, the police station dispatched telegrams to various police authorities, asking them to pay attention. At the same time, they notified all hospitals in the city to pay special attention to patients with gunshot wounds. As expected, at around 3:00 a.m. yesterday morning, a man suddenly came to Baolong Hospital on Baker Road and requested treatment for a gunshot wound on his leg. After the hospital made detailed inquiries, it was said that his name was Hu

Rongsheng, 24 years old, from Shandong, and lived on Tailasite Road in the French Concession. When asked why he was injured, he was vague. The hospital suspected him

and reported it to the police station. The police were dispatched to the hospital and took him to the police hospital. The bullet was removed from his leg, and after examination, it was indeed the bullet fired by the two police officers, No. 3002 and No. 2480. Knowing that he was the bandit they were searching for, they immediately placed him under surveillance.

Another Escaped Bandit Captured: Not long after, the police station suddenly received a call from the French police station, saying that there was a man with a gunshot wound in the abdomen at Guangci Hospital on Jin Shenfu Road. He was seeking treatment at the hospital with evasive language and had been detained by the police station. After receiving the report, the Public Concession Police Station rushed to bring the man back and sent him to the police hospital for treatment. After examination by the hospital doctor, it was found that he was also the escaped bandit, so he was also placed under surveillance. When asked his name, he said that his name was Xu Wenzhuo, 22 years old, and lived on Taoerfeisi Road in the French Concession. He also confessed that he had gone to rob and opened fire to resist arrest. There were a total of three bandits who went with him that day. Therefore, the police station is still strictly pursuing the escaped bandit. As of the time the reporter drafted the manuscript, it was learned that a clue had been obtained.

Inland River Thaws, Ships Resume Navigation

But Due to the Cold Weather, Travel is Slightly Slower Than Before

Wusong River Blocked, Changed Course

After heavy snow in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, the inland river shipping was interrupted due to the freezing of the waterways. In addition, the siltation of the Suzhou River became increasingly serious, blocking the ships. Now, all inland river ships have completely resumed navigation. However, ships in Wuxi, Qingpu, and other places have changed course to the South Huangpu River. The details are recorded as follows:

Thawing and Resumption of Navigation: Merchant Shipping, Ning Shao, Gong Mao, Xie Xing, Tai Dong, Yuan Tong, Rui Shengxiang, Li Xing, and other inland river shipping companies operating ships on the Shanghai-Hangzhou, Shanghai-Huzhou, Shanghai-Wuxi, Shanghai-Suzhou, Shanghai-Zhangjiagang, Shanghai-Qingpu, and other routes. Previously, due to heavy snow in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, the waterways were frozen, causing ships to Qingpu, Changshu, Changzhou, Wuxi, and other places to stop sailing. Ships to Hangzhou, Huzhou, and other places were delayed each time. After the ships tried to break the ice and with continuous sunny days, the waterways thawed, and inland river ships in all places have completely resumed navigation. However, due to the cold weather, travel is slightly slower than usual.

Changing Course: As for the Wusong River, due to the increasing siltation, as the lunar New Year is approaching, ships from various villages are sailing to Shanghai to purchase

goods or sell goods, which is very crowded, causing ships at the Shanban Factory Bridge and other places to be congested. Ships sailing to Shanghai-Wuxi and Shanghai-Qingpu are changing course to the South Huangpu River each time they set sail. However, the journey is about 100 li longer than the original route, so they must arrive late, causing the schedule to be disrupted. It is reported that the trade association has requested that measures be taken to dredge the river to facilitate transportation.

Report on the Embezzlement Case of Over 80,000 at the Consolidated Tax Bureau to the Ministry of Finance: Discovery Process

Subordinate Staff Deng Darong's Account of the Origin of the Embezzlement

Bureau Chief Wang Zongzhu Voluntarily Requests Punishment for Negligence

According to the Dagong News Agency, Deng Darong, a second-class staff member of the Suzhou-Zhejiang-Anhui Consolidated Tax Bureau in this city, forged the Bureau Chief's seal and fraudulently obtained over 80,000 yuan in tax funds from the Central Bank. This was discovered at the end of last year during the year-end settlement. The Bureau had already detained Deng and sent him to the local court for interrogation, as previously reported. Bureau Chief Wang Zongzhu, considering the seriousness of the matter, yesterday submitted a detailed report of the incident

to the Ministry of Finance and the Tax Affairs Department, requesting review. The original text obtained is as follows: (Omitted above) Upon investigation, the tax funds collected by the various inspection offices under this Bureau were previously remitted to the Bureau in cash, or transferred to the Bureau through banks for verification and receipt, and were uniformly deposited in the Bank of Communications for safekeeping and remittance. Since April of the 20th year of the Republic (1931), after the implementation of the "Regulations for the Central Bank to Manage the Collection and Remittance of Consolidated Taxes" as ordered by the former Consolidated Tax Department, or through other entrusted commercial firms,

funds were transferred to the Shanghai Head Office. Each month, a document was falsely submitted to the Bureau for inclusion in the receipts. However, at that time, the Central Bank only had a consolidated tax account and no account for this Bureau. In August of the same year, an order was received from the Department, through a notification from the Central Bank Business Bureau, stating that the tax funds remitted by the inspection offices were part of this Bureau's income. Although the offices were directly remitting funds to the Central Bank Business Bureau in accordance with the regulations, according to the supervisory system, the Bureau should still

review and include the amount in the accounts

and submit a supplementary document for verification in order to correct the accounting. The Bureau immediately reported this to the former Consolidated Tax Department, which approved a letter to the Central Bank Business Bureau, referring to the method of the Shandong-Henan Consolidated Tax Bureau, to open a separate account for this Bureau. All tax funds remitted by the offices under the Bureau's jurisdiction should first be included in this Bureau's account, and then transferred to the Department by the Bureau issuing checks. Consequently, on September 23 of the same year, two signed seals were sent to the Central Bank Business Bureau for record. This was the beginning of the establishment of an account for this Bureau's tax funds in the Central Bank. According to the "Regulations for the Central Bank to Manage the Collection and Remittance of Funds for the Ministry of Finance's Consolidated Tax Department,"

Article 10 stated: "The seal for withdrawing funds from the Consolidated Tax Department shall be signed and issued by the Consolidated Tax Department and the local consolidated tax bureaus or inspection offices. All checks shall also be kept separately. Furthermore, the checks of each bureau or office shall only be signed and used when remitting funds on the 25th of each month. No checks may be signed or withdrawn in addition to what is specified.” Therefore, when this Bureau remitted these tax funds each month, the checks issued by the bases specified "Pay to the order of" followed by "Tax Affairs Department" on the check, and the words "or bearer" were crossed out, indicating that the amount of the check was specifically for transferring funds to the Tax Affairs Department account. The checks were

personally signed

and stamped with the ivory seal bearing the two characters "Zong Zhu". This ivory seal was specifically for signing checks for remitting funds. Now, upon investigation, Deng Darong, an auditor in the First Section of this Bureau, has been responsible for handling the remittance of various tax funds and auditing the remittance affairs of various branch offices. The disposition and regulations have been established accordingly. Therefore, the number of remittances submitted to the Bureau by the various inspection offices and the number listed in the Bureau's Central Bank account are all audited by this staff member. When this Bureau prepares a document at the end of the month to remit funds to the Department, the cashier also sends the check to this staff member for checking, filling in the details, and returning it for signing and remittance to the Department. This staff member rarely took leave, except for a few days of sick leave before the New Year holiday. On the 4th of the month, he had not yet returned from leave. On that day, the Nanjing Inspection Office submitted the December wheat flour tax. Because the staff member was on leave, the remittance document and attachments were received by the cashier. The cashier, noting that the remittance was for the December wheat flour tax, checked the records and found that the Nanjing Inspection Office had only remitted wheat flour tax up to October. The cashier inquired why the Central Bank had not yet listed the November tax, and after an investigation, it was discovered that the bank had already listed the November tax, but this Bureau's records did not include this amount, indicating an apparent irregularity. Upon further inquiry, it was learned that someone had repeatedly withdrawn cash from the Central Bank, and the Central Bank provided the cash withdrawal checks for review. The seal and signature

did not match.

It was determined that someone had fraudulently withdrawn the funds. Upon examining the back of the check, it was discovered to be stamped with the "Duan Ji" seal and a receipt stamp from the Shanghai China Agricultural and Industrial Bank. Furthermore, it was discovered that Deng Darong had issued checks under the name of "Duan Ji" from the Agricultural and Industrial Bank, which had been seen by the Bureau's staff. The fraudulent signature was clearly the work of this staff member. Subsequently, it was discovered that this staff member had secretly gone to Guangdong during his leave and returned to Shanghai on the Empress of Asia ship on the 6th of this month. Therefore, people were secretly dispatched to wait and bring him in for questioning. The staff member was immediately dismissed and sent to the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau for custody. A report was made to the Tax Affairs Department, and auditors Chen Jun and Lü Chunming were dispatched to the Bureau to jointly open the staff member's official iron cabinet and the drawers of his residence. A forged stone seal and Central Bank checkbook, deposit slips, and other items were found. In addition, three remittance documents from the Hangzhou Inspection Office and two from the Changzhou

Inspection Office, as well as one remittance document from the Nanjing Inspection Office, totaling six documents, were found unfiled. A batch of Central Bank Business Bureau receipts and payment notices were also concealed and seized. As for this Bureau's account at the Central Bank,

according to regulations, the Bureau could only issue checks for

transferring funds to the Department and could not withdraw cash. Furthermore, the only deposits

were remittances from various inspection offices, and no cash deposits were made. The staff member's duty was only to audit the amounts. However, in the staff member's iron cabinet and drawers, a forged seal, check stubs, and deposit slips were found. When questioned about where the seal and checks came from, how he was able to withdraw cash from the Central Bank, and how he delivered the cash, he claimed: "In April of the 21st year of the Republic (1932), due to a temporary need, I planned to secretly withdraw tax funds from the Central Bank. I secretly carved a Bureau Chief's seal in advance. When filling out checks for remitting funds, I secretly stole the check receipt form from the checkbook and fraudulently obtained a checkbook from the Central Bank. I filled out two checks, stamped them with the secretly carved seal, and withdrew cash from the Central Bank. The Central Bank initially

refused to pay because the seal did not match.

I then signed two more checks, still using the secretly carved seal, and sent a letter to the Central Bank in the name of the Bureau Chief, requesting payment. This letter was also stamped with the secretly carved seal, and the Central Bank then paid. From then on, I obtained a Central Bank checkbook for this Bureau's account. I continued to use the secretly carved seal to fraudulently obtain cash from the Central Bank. Later, fearing that this would be discovered during the mid-year settlement in June, I devised methods to cover it up. Because the Bureau's remittances are required to be completed in full each month, and the various inspection offices are located at different distances, it often takes almost a month to complete the full remittance. At that time, the next month's tax funds from the inspection offices near Shanghai may also be remitted. Therefore, I delayed sending the remittance documents from the offices near Shanghai to the cashier, so that the cashier's daily report could not include them, and the accounting department also

could not record them.

In this way, although the funds had arrived at the bank and the documents had arrived at the Bureau, the cashier, accounting, and auditing departments of this Bureau had no way of knowing. I was then able to move funds from the future to cover for the past. During the account reconciliation in June and at the end of the year (i.e., semi-annual), if there were discrepancies in the amounts, I would fraudulently withdraw more funds or return some cash to the Central Bank to ensure that the bank's deposit balance matched the amount listed in the Bureau's account for the half-year settlement, preventing the Bureau's departments from discovering it. As for the amount overdrawn, because it has been a long time, I cannot remember. I know that this is a capital crime, and I only ask for leniency." Upon examining the situation, the ingenuity of the scheme and the skill of the cover-up are beyond the expectations of ordinary people. The Bureau Chief believes that, according to regulations, this account at the Central Bank can only be transferred for remittance and cannot be withdrawn

in cash. I never expected that this staff member would dare to forge a seal and fraudulently obtain funds.

It is truly regrettable.

As for the amount overdrawn, we will discuss with the Central Bank and request that the account statements of this Bureau from the opening of the account to the end of the 22nd year of the Republic (1933) be copied and sent to us. We will then compare them in detail with the Bureau's general ledger. It is estimated that a total of 84,348.28 yuan in taxes was fraudulently obtained. Furthermore, the staff member returned 27.07 yuan to the Central Bank, so the actual amount fraudulently withdrawn was 84,321.21 yuan. According to the records, the Hangzhou Inspection Office remitted 154.70 yuan for the November wheat flour tax in the 22nd year of the Republic (1933). Furthermore, the Hangzhou Inspection Office remitted 13,457.43 yuan for the same month's cotton yarn tax, and the Hangzhou Inspection Office remitted 25,500 yuan for the same month's match tax. Furthermore, the Changzhou Inspection Office remitted 3,211.27 yuan for the same month's wheat flour tax, and the Changzhou Inspection Office remitted 31,771.22 yuan for the same month's cotton yarn tax. Furthermore, the Nanjing Inspection Office remitted 10,226.59 yuan for the same month's wheat tax, totaling 84,321.21 yuan,

which precisely matches the amount of the staff member's fraudulent withdrawal from the Central Bank. This is the result of the investigation of the staff member's forgery of the seal and

fraudulent obtainment of tax funds.

In summary, the staff member fraudulently obtained 84,321.21 yuan in taxes. When he was detained, he turned over 212 yuan in Shanghai banknotes and 750 yuan in Hong Kong banknotes. Furthermore, it was discovered that the staff member had accounts under the name of "Duan Ji" at the Shanghai China Agricultural and Industrial Bank, which could be recovered for a total of 13,001.20 yuan. The remaining amount is 71,358.01 yuan. The staff member's forgery of the seal and fraudulent withdrawal of tax funds are confirmed by evidence and testimony. He has disregarded the law and should be severely punished to serve as a warning. The Bureau Chief's improper use of personnel and failure to detect the crime is inexcusable and should be subject to strict disciplinary action.

The above-mentioned situation of this case was first submitted by the Bureau Chief to the Minister of Finance for review. The Minister instructed that the staff member be transferred to the court for interrogation and prosecution. Following this instruction, on the 15th of this month, a letter was sent to the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau, requesting that the staff member be transferred to the Shanghai First Special District Local Court for interrogation. In addition to dispatching personnel to the First Special District Local Court to file a lawsuit and attach a civil suit with various evidence, and to report the court's interrogation situation at any time after the prosecution, a document is submitted to request review of the case of Deng Darong, a staff member of this Bureau, forging a seal and fraudulently obtaining tax funds from the bank, and the process of transferring him to the court for interrogation in accordance with the instruction. In addition to submitting this to the Minister of Finance, this is respectfully submitted to the Tax Affairs Department of the Ministry of Finance.

Low Water Levels in the Yangtze River: Strict Precautions Against Banditry on Salt Barges

Upper Yangtze Shallow Water Fees Increased by 50%

Since the Yangtze River's upstream water level has dropped significantly, the river's water is only five chi deep. Ships traveling to Hunan have all been forced to stop, and goods are being transferred to barges. The Hongzhen and Hongting, two vessels of the Sanbei Company, were transporting salt into Hunan on this trip. They should have already arrived since departing from Hankou. However, yesterday, the Shashi Branch sent a telegram stating that the Hongzhen and Hongheng ships had not yet arrived. The Juyan Salt Warehouse is very anxious about this. During periods of shallow water, riverboats are often stopped, and bandits in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, due to the central government's blockade, lack salt and pay special attention to salt transport ships. If they are stranded for a long time, there is a risk of banditry. The Shashi Branch of the Juyan Salt Warehouse should quickly dispatch barges to transport the salt from the Hongzhen and Hongheng ships as soon as possible to avoid danger. Yesterday, the Sanbei Company ordered the Hankou Branch to quickly send a tow barge to transport the salt.

The six Shanghai companies' upper Yangtze shallow water fees were originally increased by 30% on the 13th of last month. Because the water level has been falling daily and ship navigation is difficult, it was publicly agreed yesterday that the previous 30% increase would be abolished and replaced with a 50% surcharge based on the fixed price, with the funds being used for operational support.

Update on the French Municipal Council's Suspension of Rickshaw Licenses

Rickshaw Merchants Continue to Petition the Taxpayers' Association

Industry Association Announces Registration

According to Guowen News Agency, the French Municipal Council's restriction on rickshaw licenses has resulted in a portion of small-scale rickshaw merchants in the French Concession being unable to obtain January licenses. As a result, over 2,000 rickshaw pullers who rely on this for a living have become unemployed. Rickshaw merchants, in particular, are complaining bitterly and are requesting the Shanghai Rickshaw Industry Association to find a solution. The Association, fearing that unemployment would lead to trouble, has been holding meetings to discuss countermeasures while also comforting the unemployed rickshaw merchants and pullers, urging them to remain calm and refrain from any rash actions. The Association has also petitioned higher authorities for intervention and has elected representatives to petition the Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the French Concession, requesting them to appeal to the French authorities in order to achieve the goal of issuing supplementary licenses. Furthermore, in order to comply with Chairman Cheng of the Taxpayers' Association, a detailed report was submitted yesterday to investigate the unemployed rickshaws and conduct registration. The submitted registration form is as follows:

Petition to the Taxpayers' Association: We are submitting a further petition requesting your review and assistance. The number of operating rickshaws in this city is limited to 10,000 by the Shanghai Municipal Council in the International Settlement. In the Chinese areas of Nanshi, Beishi, Pudong, and Huxi, the Public Utilities Bureau has set a limit of 10,000. The French Concession, located between the Chinese and British areas, has never had a fixed number of rickshaw licenses. While the British Settlement issues licenses in numbered order up to 10,000, and the Chinese area of Nanshi has 6,014 rickshaws, approximately 5,000 rickshaws supplementally obtain French licenses due to their proximity. Since the January 28th Incident in the past, some rickshaw merchants from Zhabei moved to Nanshi to operate. Furthermore, unlicensed rickshaws in the Caojiadu area of Huxi have been expanded from 600-700 to over 3,100 by the Public Utilities Bureau in the name of reorganization, and the French Concession in Xuhui and Xinhua Districts has been designated as their operating area. More of these rickshaws also obtain French licenses for compensation. As a result, the number of French licenses, which was previously around 5,000 in addition to the Special District, has been increasing daily. In order to maintain traffic, the French authorities have stipulated that, in addition to the 10,000 British licenses, the maximum number is 7,000. This is not a problem during the summer and autumn months, as most rickshaw pullers return to their hometowns to farm. However, during the cold winter months, many impoverished laborers and bankrupt farmers from northern Jiangsu come to Shanghai, and there are even more people who rely on pulling rickshaws for a living. This creates a shortage of the 7,000 rickshaw licenses. Therefore, all 7,000 rickshaw licenses for November and December of last year were eagerly snatched up within three to five days. This year, the French authorities stipulated that old licenses from December 1933 would be exchanged for new licenses for January 1934. Furthermore, starting this month, all those with January rickshaw licenses have been ordered to provide a guarantor and pay the fees. However, rickshaw merchants have had French licenses for 300-400 rickshaws, and now they have suddenly been suspended, resulting in approximately 2,000-3,000 pullers sharing five or six rickshaws losing their livelihoods. The rickshaw merchants are suffering losses because their empty rickshaws parked outside their doors are subject to police intervention. Therefore, the losses suffered by rickshaw merchants over the past two months are countless. In the past, merchants still naively hoped that the French authorities would take care of the rickshaw owners who have been paying operating fees for many years. However, after two months, this hope has been dashed. Thousands of rickshaw pullers have lost their homes due to the suspension of business, and dozens of small businesses, on which more than a thousand people depend for food and clothing, are in constant anxiety. If a solution is not found soon, it will be related to social order and the livelihoods of the poor. Therefore, we are submitting a detailed report of the situation, as well as a copy of the registration form, and respectfully request your association to forward it to the French Municipal Council, to review the donation records and provide remedies to save the livelihoods of the poor and maintain social stability. The merchants will be extremely grateful and will wait for your instructions. Respectfully submitted to the Chairman of the Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the French Concession. The Shanghai Rickshaw Industry Association, Rickshaw Merchant Representatives Li Pingyu, Yu Shanjiang, Jiang Heshang, Chen Changsheng, Liu Qikuan, Zhou Jungong, Zhang Zhengkui, Li Wanzhang, and others, jointly submitted on January 24, 23rd year of the Republic (1934).

Investigation and Registration: The Shanghai Rickshaw Industry Association is investigating and registering the names of those whose rickshaw licenses have been suspended by the French authorities: Chen Changsheng 17, Yu Shanjiang 7, Xu Huangfu 10, Zhu Qiyuan 2, Fan Youkuan 5, Chen Yousi 1, Xu Kaiyou 2, Zhu Baohuan 6, Li Pingyu 40, Wang Dengcai 6, Li Helong 1, Liu Dasan 1, Xu Xiangji 2, Wang Bixi 4, Xiong Chunhua 4, Ju Ganxin 17, Liu Changjiang 8, Liu Zhengyin 5, Chen Fujiang 11, Zhang Gui 3, Liu Guang'an 1, Cao Asan 1, Xu Shurong 1, Yuan Dehua 1, Wang Huaiyi 1, Lü Xiushan 7, Ma Chunhong 2, Zhou Jungong 9, Zhang Zhengkui 3, Wu Jixiang 6, Wu Chongyin 1, Jiang Ruiliang 12, Tian Jingen 2, Wang Fengyou 2, Ma Chengfang 4, An Genlin 16, Chen Jinshan 7, Li Zhiliang 40, Su Genlin 3, Gu Changsheng 3, Sun Zhaofang 1, Zhang Huailin 2, Chen Shouchang 9, Wang Taikang 5, Zhao Yougao 4, Chen Guolin 1, Xie Zhengfang 1, Li Wanzhang 1, Chen Xin 10, Zhu Qiming 1, Wu Wanqing 1, Jiang Jianqun 9, Shen Yousheng 3, Liu Qikuan 24. The above total is 346 vehicles, with the majority owning only one vehicle.

Shanghai Municipal Council Discusses Tax Exemption Cases

The Shanghai Municipal Council's Finance Committee recently discussed several requests for tax exemption. One case involved a subordinate temple of a Buddhist temple at 476 Avenue Edward VII, with an estimated annual rental value of 3,600 yuan and a quarterly tax of 126 yuan. The location is a five-bay Chinese-style urban building, with only the upper floor being used for religious purposes. The Committee stated that tax exemptions for temples must be for buildings located in sacred places and not used for other purposes, so the request should not be approved. Another case involved a request for tax exemption for a portion of 0A310 Dongjiaxing Road, which was intended for private worship. The Committee found that the location did not meet the requirements for tax exemption and was also being used for commercial activities, so it also recommended disapproval. Another case involved a dispute over the estimated rental value of 15,600 yuan for a warehouse at 784 and 796 North Suzhou Road. The Committee decided to uphold the original assessment. All of the above cases have been approved by the Board of Directors on Wednesday of this week and will be implemented accordingly.

A Total of 560,000 Yuan, One Month's Salary per Person

The Two Railways Union Has Understood and There Are No Problems

The Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways Administration had an operating income of over 20 million yuan last year, with a net profit of approximately 3 million yuan.
